1138:         <div class="paper-section">
1139:           <h3 class="paper-title"><span class="hi">PSC-C-208: पाश्चात्य राजनीतिक विचार</span><span class="en">PSC-C-208:
1140:               Western Political Thought</span></h3>
1141: 
1142:           <h4 class="unit-title"><span class="hi">इकाई 1 एवं 2: प्लेटो और अरस्तू</span><span class="en">Unit 1 & 2:
1143:               Plato and Aristotle</span></h4>
1144:           <ul>
1145:             <li><strong><span class="hi">प्लेटो (Plato):</span><span class="en">Plato:</span></strong> <span
1146:                 class="hi">द रिपब्लिक (The Republic) के लेखक। <strong>दार्शनिक-राजा (Philosopher-King)</strong> का
1147:                 समर्थन किया। उन्होंने शासकों (अभिभावकों) को भ्रष्टाचार से दूर रखने के लिए <strong>'निजी संपत्ति और
1148:                   परिवार के साम्यवाद' (Abolition of property/family)</strong> का सुझाव दिया। उनका 'नोबल लाई' (Noble Lie
1149:                 - धातुओं का मिथक) सामाजिक स्थिरता के लिए था।</span><span class="en">Author of The Republic. Advocated
1150:                 for the <strong>Philosopher-King</strong>. He suggested the <strong>'Communism of wives and property'
1151:                   (Abolition of property/family)</strong> for the guardians to keep them free from corruption. His
1152:                 'Noble Lie' (Myth of Metals) was for social stability.</span></li>
1153:             <li><strong><span class="hi">अरस्तू (Aristotle):</span><span class="en">Aristotle:</span></strong> <span
1154:                 class="hi">राजनीति विज्ञान के जनक। उनका प्रसिद्ध कथन है "मनुष्य स्वभाव से एक राजनीतिक प्राणी है।" उनका
1155:                 आदर्श <strong>पॉलिटी (Polity)</strong> है, जो कुलीनतंत्र और लोकतंत्र का मिश्रित रूप है, जहाँ मध्यम वर्ग
1156:                 स्थिरता प्रदान करता है।</span><span class="en">Father of Political Science. His famous statement is "Man
1157:                 is by nature a political animal." His ideal state is <strong>Polity</strong>, a mixed form of oligarchy
1158:                 and democracy, where the middle class provides stability.</span></li>
1159:           </ul>
1160: 
1161:           <h4 class="unit-title"><span class="hi">इकाई 4: मैकियावेली — आधुनिक विचारक</span><span class="en">Unit 4:
1162:               Machiavelli — Modern Thinker</span></h4>
1163:           <p><span class="hi">निकोलो मैकियावेली की प्रसिद्ध पुस्तक <strong>'द प्रिंस' (1513)</strong> है। उन्होंने
1164:               राजनीति को नैतिकता और धर्म से अलग किया (राजनीतिक यथार्थवाद)। 'प्रिंस' को शेर (बल) और लोमड़ी (चालाकी) दोनों
1165:               होना चाहिए। उनका मानना था कि <strong>"साध्य साधनों को उचित ठहराता है" (The end justifies the
1166:                 means)</strong>।</span><span class="en">Niccolò Machiavelli's famous book is <strong>'The Prince'
1167:                 (1513)</strong>. He separated politics from morality and religion (Political Realism). A 'Prince' must
1168:               be both a lion (force) and a fox (cunning). He believed that <strong>"The end justifies the
1169:                 means"</strong>.</span></p>
1170: 
1171:           <h4 class="unit-title"><span class="hi">इकाई 6 और 10: जे.एस. मिल और कार्ल मार्क्स</span><span class="en">Unit
1172:               6 and 10: J.S. Mill and Karl Marx</span></h4>
1173:           <ul>
1174:             <li><strong><span class="hi">जे. एस. मिल (J. S. Mill - स्वतंत्रता):</span><span class="en">J. S. Mill
1175:                   (Liberty):</span></strong> <span class="hi">उनकी पुस्तक <em>'ऑन लिबर्टी' (1859)</em> में <strong>हानि
1176:                   सिद्धांत (Harm Principle)</strong> दिया गया है: "किसी व्यक्ति की इच्छा के विरुद्ध शक्ति का प्रयोग करने
1177:                 का एकमात्र उद्देश्य दूसरों को नुकसान से बचाना है।"</span><span class="en">His book <em>'On Liberty'
1178:                   (1859)</em> introduces the <strong>Harm Principle</strong>: "The only purpose for which power can be
1179:                 rightfully exercised over any member of a civilized community, against his will, is to prevent harm to
1180:                 others."</span></li>
1181:             <li><strong><span class="hi">कार्ल मार्क्स (Karl Marx):</span><span class="en">Karl Marx:</span></strong>
1182:               <span class="hi"><strong>ऐतिहासिक भौतिकवाद (Historical Materialism):</strong> इतिहास का निर्धारण
1183:                 आर्थिक/भौतिक स्थितियों द्वारा होता है (हेगेल के विचारवाद का उलटा)। <strong>अधिशेष मूल्य (Surplus
1184:                   Value):</strong> श्रमिक अपने वेतन से अधिक मूल्य पैदा करते हैं, जिसे पूंजीपति हड़प लेता है; यही शोषण
1185:                 है। मार्क्स का लक्ष्य एक 'वर्गविहीन और राज्यविहीन' (Classless and stateless) कम्युनिस्ट समाज की स्थापना
1186:                 था।</span><span class="en"><strong>Historical Materialism:</strong> History is determined by
1187:                 economic/material conditions (an inversion of Hegel's idealism). <strong>Surplus Value:</strong> Workers
1188:                 produce more value than their wages, which the capitalist appropriates; this is exploitation. Marx's
1189:                 goal was the establishment of a 'classless and stateless' communist society.</span></li>
1190:           </ul>
1191:         </div>
1192: 
1193:         <!-- PHASE 12: SEMESTER 2 MASTER Q&A & TIPS -->
1194:         <div class="paper-section" id="sem2-qa">
1195:           <h3 class="paper-title" style="background: linear-gradient(135deg, #10b981 0%, #059669 100%); color: white;">
1196:             <i class="fas fa-trophy"></i>
1197:             <span class="hi">सेमेस्टर II - मास्टर Q&A और UGC NET टिप्स</span>
1198:             <span class="en">Semester II - Master Q&A & UGC NET Tips</span>
1199:           </h3>
1200: 
1201:           <p class="intro-text">
1202:             <span class="hi">परीक्षा में सर्वोच्च अंक (Gold Medal) और JRF के लिए अति-महत्वपूर्ण प्रश्न।</span>
1203:             <span class="en">Highly important questions for Gold Medal in University exams and JRF.</span>
1204:           </p>
1205: 
1206:           <!-- PAPER 1 (Academic Writing) -->
1207:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Academic Writing and Communication Skills</h4>
1208:           <div class="content-box">
1209:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1210:             <ol>
1211:               <li><strong>What is a Research Synopsis?</strong> A blueprint or summary of proposed research detailing the problem, objectives, and methodology.</li>
1212:               <li><strong>What does APA stand for and where is it used?</strong> American Psychological Association; used primarily in Social Sciences.</li>
1213:               <li><strong>Explain the 'Author-Date' citation system.</strong> In-text citations include the author's last name and publication year, e.g., (Smith, 2020).</li>
1214:               <li><strong>What is Plagiarism?</strong> The unethical practice of presenting someone else's work or ideas as your own without proper acknowledgment.</li>
1215:               <li><strong>What is a Literature Review?</strong> A critical analysis of existing published research relevant to your topic.</li>
1216:             </ol>
1217:             <p><strong>Top 2 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1218:             <ul>
1219:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Define Academic Writing and discuss its key characteristics compared to creative writing.</li>
1220:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Explain the different standard Citation Styles (APA, MLA, Chicago). Why is proper citation essential in research?</li>
1221:             </ul>
1222:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1223:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1224:               <p>For Research Aptitude (Paper 1), remember: APA is Author-Date (Social Sciences). MLA is Author-Page (Humanities). Chicago uses Footnotes/Endnotes (History).</p>
1225:             </div>
1226:           </div>
1227: 
1228:           <!-- PAPER 2 (International Relations) -->
1229:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Theories of International Politics</h4>
1230:           <div class="content-box">
1231:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1232:             <ol>
1233:               <li><strong>What is 'Classical Realism'?</strong> Hans Morgenthau's theory that states act out of a natural human desire for power.</li>
1234:               <li><strong>What is 'Neo-Realism'?</strong> Kenneth Waltz's theory that the anarchic structure of the international system, not human nature, dictates state behavior.</li>
1235:               <li><strong>Define 'Balance of Power'.</strong> A mechanism where states form alliances to prevent any single state from becoming dominant.</li>
1236:               <li><strong>What is 'Collective Security'?</strong> An arrangement (like the UN) where an attack on one state is treated as an attack on all.</li>
1237:               <li><strong>What is the core argument of Constructivism?</strong> Alexander Wendt argued that "Anarchy is what states make of it"—international relations are socially constructed by ideas and norms.</li>
1238:             </ol>
1239:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1240:             <ul>
1241:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Critically examine Hans Morgenthau’s Six Principles of Political Realism.</li>
1242:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Differentiate between Classical Realism (Morgenthau) and Structural Realism (Waltz).</li>
1243:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Analyze the relevance of the Non-Aligned Movement (NAM) in the contemporary multi-polar world.</li>
1244:             </ul>
1245:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1246:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1247:               <p>Match the book to the thinker: *Politics Among Nations* (Morgenthau), *Theory of International Politics* (Waltz), *The Tragedy of Great Power Politics* (Mearsheimer - Offensive Realism).</p>
1248:             </div>
1249:           </div>
1250: 
1251:           <!-- PAPER 3 (Public Administration) -->
1252:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Public Administration</h4>
1253:           <div class="content-box">
1254:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1255:             <ol>
1256:               <li><strong>What is the 'Hawthorne Effect'?</strong> Elton Mayo's finding that workers' productivity improves when they feel observed and valued.</li>
1257:               <li><strong>Define 'Bounded Rationality'.</strong> Herbert Simon's concept that decision-makers lack complete information and cognitive ability, so they "satisfice" instead of "optimize".</li>
1258:               <li><strong>What are the features of Weber's Ideal Bureaucracy?</strong> Hierarchy, formal rules, specialization, impersonality, and merit-based selection.</li>
1259:               <li><strong>What is the 'Prismatic-Sala' model?</strong> F.W. Riggs' model explaining administration in developing societies characterized by Formalism, Heterogeneity, and Overlapping.</li>
1260:               <li><strong>Define 'Zero-Based Budgeting' (ZBB).</strong> A budgeting method requiring every expense to be justified from 'scratch' (zero) each year.</li>
1261:             </ol>
1262:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1263:             <ul>
1264:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Evaluate Herbert Simon's Decision-Making Approach in Public Administration.</li>
1265:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Critically analyze Max Weber’s theory of Bureaucracy. Discuss Robert Merton's critique of it.</li>
1266:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Examine the concept, evolution, and core principles of New Public Administration (NPA).</li>
1267:             </ul>
1268:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1269:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1270:               <p>Keywords mapping: "Satisficing" = Simon. "Prismatic/Sala" = Riggs. "Scientific Management" = Taylor. "Social Equity/Minnowbrook" = NPA (Frederickson).</p>
1271:             </div>
1272:           </div>
1273: 
1274:           <!-- PAPER 4 (Western Political Thought / Indian Political System) -->
1275:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Indian Political System & Western Thought</h4>
1276:           <div class="content-box">
1277:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1278:             <ol>
1279:               <li><strong>What is the 'Basic Structure Doctrine'?</strong> Established in Kesavananda Bharati (1973), it prevents Parliament from altering the fundamental features of the Constitution.</li>
1280:               <li><strong>Define 'Judicial Activism'.</strong> The judiciary playing a proactive role to protect citizen rights (e.g., through PILs).</li>
1281:               <li><strong>What is Aristotle's classification of the State?</strong> He classified states by the number of rulers and their intent (Rule of One: Monarchy/Tyranny; Rule of Few: Aristocracy/Oligarchy; Rule of Many: Polity/Democracy).</li>
1282:               <li><strong>What is J.S. Mill's 'Harm Principle'?</strong> State intervention is only justified to prevent an individual from harming others.</li>
1283:               <li><strong>What is Marx's 'Historical Materialism'?</strong> The theory that economic structures (the base) shape all political and social institutions (the superstructure).</li>
1284:             </ol>
1285:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1286:             <ul>
1287:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> "The Indian Constitution is federal in form but unitary in spirit." Discuss.</li>
1288:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Analyze Machiavelli's advice to a ruler as outlined in 'The Prince'. Why is he considered the first modern political thinker?</li>
1289:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Discuss Karl Marx's theory of Class Struggle and Surplus Value.</li>
1290:             </ul>
1291:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1292:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1293:               <p>For Indian Polity, remember Art 32 (5 Writs), Art 143 (Advisory Jurisdiction), Art 356 (President's Rule). For Western Thought, remember Machiavelli separated Politics from Ethics/Religion.</p>
1294:             </div>
1295:           </div>
1296:         </div>
1297:       </div>

1300:       <div id="sem3" class="tab-pane">
1301:         <h2 class="semester-title"><span class="hi">सेमेस्टर III — ऐच्छिक पाठ्यक्रम</span><span class="en">Semester III
1302:             — Elective Courses</span></h2>
1303: 
1304:         <!-- Paper 309 -->
1305:         <div class="paper-section">
1306:           <h3 class="paper-title"><span class="hi">PSC-A-309: मानवाधिकार</span><span class="en">PSC-A-309: Human
1307:               Rights</span></h3>
1308:           <p><span class="hi">मानवाधिकार वे अहरणीय (Inalienable) अधिकार हैं जो प्रत्येक व्यक्ति को केवल इंसान होने के
1309:               नाते प्राप्त हैं।</span><span class="en">Human rights are inalienable rights inherent to all human beings,
1310:               regardless of race, sex, nationality, ethnicity, language, religion, or any other status.</span></p>
1311:           <div class="info-box">
1312:             <h4><span class="hi">मानवाधिकारों की तीन पीढ़ियां (करेल वासक द्वारा)</span><span class="en">Three
1313:                 Generations of Human Rights (by Karel Vasak)</span></h4>
1314:             <ul>
1315:               <li><strong><span class="hi">पहली पीढ़ी (नागरिक और राजनीतिक अधिकार):</span><span class="en">First
1316:                     Generation (Civil and Political Rights):</span></strong> <span class="hi">स्वतंत्रता से संबंधित
1317:                   (जैसे, अभिव्यक्ति की स्वतंत्रता)। इन्हें नकारात्मक अधिकार माना जाता है क्योंकि राज्य को हस्तक्षेप करने
1318:                   से रोका जाता है।</span><span class="en">Relating to liberty (e.g., freedom of speech). Considered
1319:                   negative rights because they prevent state interference.</span></li>
1320:               <li><strong><span class="hi">दूसरी पीढ़ी (आर्थिक, सामाजिक और सांस्कृतिक अधिकार):</span><span
1321:                     class="en">Second Generation (Economic, Social & Cultural Rights):</span></strong> <span
1322:                   class="hi">समानता से संबंधित (जैसे, काम का अधिकार, शिक्षा का अधिकार)। इन्हें सकारात्मक अधिकार माना
1323:                   जाता है क्योंकि राज्य को इन्हें सुनिश्चित करना होता है।</span><span class="en">Relating to equality
1324:                   (e.g., right to work, education). Considered positive rights because the state must provide
1325:                   them.</span></li>
1326:               <li><strong><span class="hi">तीसरी पीढ़ी (सामूहिक/एकजुटता अधिकार):</span><span class="en">Third Generation
1327:                     (Collective/Solidarity Rights):</span></strong> <span class="hi">बंधुत्व से संबंधित (जैसे, स्वच्छ
1328:                   पर्यावरण का अधिकार, विकास का अधिकार)।</span><span class="en">Relating to fraternity (e.g., right to a
1329:                   clean environment, right to development).</span></li>
1330:             </ul>
1331:           </div>
1332:           <ul>
1333:             <li><strong><span class="hi">UDHR (1948):</span><span class="en">UDHR (1948):</span></strong> <span
1334:                 class="hi">मानवाधिकारों की सार्वभौम घोषणा (Universal Declaration of Human Rights)। इसे 10 दिसंबर 1948 को
1335:                 UNGA द्वारा अपनाया गया (इसलिए 10 दिसंबर को मानवाधिकार दिवस मनाया जाता है)।</span><span
1336:                 class="en">Universal Declaration of Human Rights. Adopted by UNGA on 10 December 1948 (hence Human
1337:                 Rights Day is celebrated on 10th December).</span></li>
1338:             <li><strong><span class="hi">ICCPR और ICESCR (1966):</span><span class="en">ICCPR & ICESCR
1339:                   (1966):</span></strong> <span class="hi">नागरिक और राजनीतिक अधिकारों पर अंतर्राष्ट्रीय नियम (ICCPR) और
1340:                 आर्थिक, सामाजिक और सांस्कृतिक अधिकारों पर अंतर्राष्ट्रीय नियम (ICESCR)।</span><span
1341:                 class="en">International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights (ICCPR) and International Covenant on
1342:                 Economic, Social and Cultural Rights (ICESCR).</span></li>
1343:           </ul>
1344:         </div>
1345: 
1346:         <!-- Paper 310 -->
1347:         <div class="paper-section">
1348:           <h3 class="paper-title"><span class="hi">PSC-C-310: झारखंड की राजनीति</span><span class="en">PSC-C-310:
1349:               Jharkhand Politics</span></h3>
1350:           <ul>
1351:             <li><strong><span class="hi">बिरसा मुंडा का 'उलगुलान' (Ulgulan):</span><span class="en">Birsa Munda's
1352:                   'Ulgulan':</span></strong> <span class="hi">1899-1900 का महान मुंडा विद्रोह। इसके परिणामस्वरूप
1353:                 <strong>छोटानागपुर काश्तकारी अधिनियम (CNT Act, 1908)</strong> लागू हुआ, जिसने गैर-आदिवासियों (दीकुओं) को
1354:                 आदिवासी भूमि के हस्तांतरण पर रोक लगा दी।</span><span class="en">The Great Munda Rebellion of 1899-1900.
1355:                 It resulted in the <strong>Chota Nagpur Tenancy Act (CNT Act, 1908)</strong>, which prohibited the
1356:                 transfer of tribal land to non-tribals (Dikus).</span></li>
1357:             <li><strong><span class="hi">पेसा अधिनियम (PESA Act, 1996):</span><span class="en">PESA Act
1358:                   (1996):</span></strong> <span class="hi">Panchayats (Extension to Scheduled Areas) Act। यह 5वीं
1359:                 अनुसूची के क्षेत्रों (झारखंड सहित) में ग्राम सभाओं को प्राकृतिक संसाधनों पर नियंत्रण का अधिकार देकर
1360:                 आदिवासी स्वशासन को मजबूत करता है।</span><span class="en">Panchayats (Extension to Scheduled Areas) Act.
1361:                 It strengthens tribal self-governance in 5th Schedule areas (including Jharkhand) by empowering Gram
1362:                 Sabhas with control over natural resources.</span></li>
1363:             <li><strong><span class="hi">संसाधन का अभिशाप (Resource Curse):</span><span class="en">Resource
1364:                   Curse:</span></strong> <span class="hi">झारखंड खनिजों (कोयला, लोहा, अभ्रक) में समृद्ध है, लेकिन यहां
1365:                 के लोग आर्थिक रूप से पिछड़े हैं। औद्योगीकरण के कारण भारी विस्थापन हुआ है और वामपंथी उग्रवाद (नक्सलवाद)
1366:                 जैसी समस्याएं उत्पन्न हुई हैं।</span><span class="en">Jharkhand is rich in minerals (coal, iron, mica),
1367:                 but its people are economically backward. Industrialization has led to massive displacement and problems
1368:                 like Left-Wing Extremism (Naxalism).</span></li>
1369:           </ul>
1370:         </div>
1371: 
1372:         <!-- Paper 311 -->
1373:         <div class="paper-section">
1374:           <h3 class="paper-title"><span class="hi">PSC-C-311: राजनीतिक समाजशास्त्र</span><span class="en">PSC-C-311:
1375:               Political Sociology</span></h3>
1376:           <ul>
1377:             <li><strong><span class="hi">राजनीतिक समाजीकरण (Political Socialization):</span><span class="en">Political
1378:                   Socialization:</span></strong> <span class="hi">वह प्रक्रिया जिसके द्वारा नागरिक राजनीतिक मूल्यों और
1379:                 मान्यताओं को सीखते हैं। प्रमुख एजेंसियां: परिवार (सबसे महत्वपूर्ण), स्कूल, सहकर्मी समूह (Peer group) और
1380:                 मीडिया।</span><span class="en">The process by which citizens learn political values and beliefs. Main
1381:                 agencies: Family (most important), school, peer group, and media.</span></li>
1382:             <li><strong><span class="hi">राजनीतिक संस्कृति (Political Culture):</span><span class="en">Political
1383:                   Culture:</span></strong> <span class="hi">राजनीतिक व्यवस्था के प्रति लोगों के दृष्टिकोण का पैटर्न।
1384:                 गेब्रियल आमंड और सिडनी वर्बा ने अपनी पुस्तक 'द सिविक कल्चर' (1963) में इसके तीन प्रकार बताए:</span><span
1385:                 class="en">The pattern of people's attitudes towards the political system. Gabriel Almond and Sidney
1386:                 Verba in their book 'The Civic Culture' (1963) identified three types:</span>
1387:               <ol>
1388:                 <li><span class="hi">संकीर्ण (Parochial): नागरिकों को व्यवस्था की कोई जानकारी नहीं होती (उदा. पारंपरिक
1389:                     समाज)।</span><span class="en">Parochial: Citizens have no awareness of the system (e.g., traditional
1390:                     societies).</span></li>
1391:                 <li><span class="hi">अधीनस्थ (Subject): नागरिक सरकार को जानते हैं, लेकिन निर्णय लेने में भाग नहीं लेते
1392:                     (उदा. तानाशाही)।</span><span class="en">Subject: Citizens know the government but do not participate
1393:                     in decision-making (e.g., dictatorships).</span></li>
1394:                 <li><span class="hi">सहभागी (Participant): नागरिक राजनीतिक प्रक्रिया में सक्रिय रूप से भाग लेते हैं
1395:                     (उदा. मजबूत लोकतंत्र)।</span><span class="en">Participant: Citizens actively participate in the
1396:                     political process (e.g., strong democracies).</span></li>
1397:               </ol>
1398:             </li>
1399:           </ul>

1400:           <div class="info-box">
1401:             <h4><span class="hi">अभिजात वर्ग सिद्धांत (Elite Theory)</span><span class="en">Elite Theory</span></h4>
1402:             <p><span class="hi"><strong>रॉबर्ट मिशेल्स का 'अल्पतंत्र का लौह नियम' (Iron Law of Oligarchy):</strong> उनका
1403:                 दावा है कि कोई भी संगठन, चाहे वह कितना भी लोकतांत्रिक क्यों न हो, अंततः एक छोटे से कुलीन वर्ग
1404:                 (Oligarchy) द्वारा नियंत्रित हो जाता है।</span><span class="en"><strong>Robert Michels' 'Iron Law of
1405:                   Oligarchy':</strong> Claims that any organization, no matter how democratic, eventually becomes
1406:                 controlled by a small elite (Oligarchy).</span></p>
1407:             <p><span class="hi"><strong>विल्फ्रेडो पारेतो का 'अभिजात वर्ग का परिसंचरण' (Circulation of Elites):</strong>
1408:                 समाज में हमेशा शासन करने वाले अभिजात वर्ग और गैर-अभिजात वर्ग होते हैं, और सत्ता 'शेरों' (जो बल प्रयोग
1409:                 करते हैं) और 'लोमड़ियों' (जो चालाकी का प्रयोग करते हैं) के बीच घूमती रहती है।</span><span
1410:                 class="en"><strong>Vilfredo Pareto's 'Circulation of Elites':</strong> Society always has governing
1411:                 elites and non-elites, and power circulates between 'Lions' (who use force) and 'Foxes' (who use
1412:                 cunning).</span></p>
1413:           </div>
1414:         </div>
1415: 
1416:         <!-- Paper 312 -->
1417:         <div class="paper-section">
1418:           <h3 class="paper-title"><span class="hi">PSC-C-312: समकालीन राजनीतिक मुद्दे</span><span class="en">PSC-C-312:
1419:               Contemporary Political Issues</span></h3>
1420:           <ul>
1421:             <li><strong><span class="hi">उत्तर-दक्षिण विभाजन (North-South Divide):</span><span class="en">North-South
1422:                   Divide:</span></strong> <span class="hi">अमीर, विकसित देशों ('वैश्विक उत्तर') और गरीब, विकासशील देशों
1423:                 ('वैश्विक दक्षिण') के बीच सामाजिक-आर्थिक और राजनीतिक विभाजन (ब्रांट लाइन द्वारा दर्शाया
1424:                 गया)।</span><span class="en">The socio-economic and political division between rich, developed countries
1425:                 ('Global North') and poor, developing countries ('Global South') (represented by the Brandt
1426:                 Line).</span></li>
1427:             <li><strong><span class="hi">NIEO (1974):</span><span class="en">NIEO (1974):</span></strong> <span
1428:                 class="hi">नई अंतर्राष्ट्रीय आर्थिक व्यवस्था (New International Economic Order)। UNGA द्वारा पारित।
1429:                 विकासशील देशों (NAM देशों) ने मांग की कि व्यापार और वित्तीय प्रणाली को उनके पक्ष में पुनर्गठित किया
1430:                 जाए।</span><span class="en">New International Economic Order. Passed by UNGA. Developing countries (NAM
1431:                 countries) demanded that the trade and financial system be restructured in their favor.</span></li>
1432:             <li><strong><span class="hi">सतत विकास (Sustainable Development):</span><span class="en">Sustainable
1433:                   Development:</span></strong> <span class="hi"><strong>ब्रंटलैंड रिपोर्ट (1987) — 'हमारा साझा भविष्य'
1434:                   (Our Common Future):</strong> "वह विकास जो भविष्य की पीढ़ियों की अपनी जरूरतों को पूरा करने की क्षमता
1435:                 से समझौता किए बिना वर्तमान की जरूरतों को पूरा करता है।"</span><span class="en"><strong>Brundtland Report
1436:                   (1987) — 'Our Common Future':</strong> "Development that meets the needs of the present without
1437:                 compromising the ability of future generations to meet their own needs."</span></li>
1438:             <li><strong><span class="hi">CBDR (समान लेकिन विभेदित जिम्मेदारियाँ):</span><span class="en">CBDR (Common
1439:                   But Differentiated Responsibilities):</span></strong> <span class="hi">यह सिद्धांत (रियो पृथ्वी
1440:                 सम्मेलन 1992 में अपनाया गया) स्वीकार करता है कि यद्यपि सभी देशों की पर्यावरण की रक्षा करने की साझी
1441:                 जिम्मेदारी है, लेकिन विकसित देशों को अधिक बोझ उठाना चाहिए क्योंकि उन्होंने ऐतिहासिक रूप से अधिक प्रदूषण
1442:                 किया है।</span><span class="en">This principle (adopted at Rio Earth Summit 1992) acknowledges that
1443:                 while all countries share the responsibility to protect the environment, developed countries must bear a
1444:                 greater burden as they are historically responsible for more pollution.</span></li>
1445:           </ul>

1453:             <span class="en">Semester III - Master Q&A & UGC NET Tips</span>

1456:           <p class="intro-text">
1457:             <span class="hi">परीक्षा में सर्वोच्च अंक (Gold Medal) और JRF के लिए अति-महत्वपूर्ण प्रश्न।</span>

1461:           <!-- PAPER 1 (Human Rights) -->
1462:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Human Rights</h4>
1463:           <div class="content-box">
1464:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1465:             <ol>
1466:               <li><strong>What are the three generations of human rights?</strong> Karel Vasak classified them as Civil/Political (1st), Economic/Social (2nd), and Collective/Solidarity (3rd) rights.</li>
1467:               <li><strong>What is the UDHR?</strong> The Universal Declaration of Human Rights, adopted by the UN General Assembly on Dec 10, 1948.</li>
1468:               <li><strong>Difference between ICCPR and ICESCR?</strong> ICCPR covers civil/political rights (negative rights). ICESCR covers economic/social/cultural rights (positive rights requiring state action).</li>
1469:               <li><strong>What is the NHRC?</strong> The National Human Rights Commission (India), a statutory body established in 1993 to protect and promote human rights.</li>
1470:               <li><strong>Define 'inalienable rights'.</strong> Rights that cannot be taken away, given away, or transferred, as they are inherent to all human beings.</li>
1471:             </ol>
1472:             <p><strong>Top 2 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1473:             <ul>
1474:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Discuss the historical evolution of Human Rights with reference to the three generations proposed by Karel Vasak.</li>
1475:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Critically examine the Universal Declaration of Human Rights (UDHR) 1948 and its impact on global politics.</li>
1476:             </ul>
1477:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1478:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1479:               <p>Dates matter: Human Rights Day is Dec 10. NHRC established in 1993. Know that 1st generation rights correlate to "Liberty", 2nd to "Equality", and 3rd to "Fraternity".</p>
1480:             </div>
1481:           </div>
1482: 
1483:           <!-- PAPER 2 (Jharkhand Politics) -->
1484:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Jharkhand Politics</h4>
1485:           <div class="content-box">
1486:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1487:             <ol>
1488:               <li><strong>What was the Birsa Munda 'Ulgulan'?</strong> The Great Rebellion (1899-1900) by Birsa Munda against British agrarian policies and non-tribal landlords.</li>
1489:               <li><strong>What is the CNT Act 1908?</strong> The Chota Nagpur Tenancy Act restricts the transfer of tribal land to non-tribals to prevent exploitation.</li>
1490:               <li><strong>Define the 'Resource Curse' in Jharkhand.</strong> The paradox where Jharkhand has massive mineral wealth but suffers from extreme poverty and underdevelopment.</li>
1491:               <li><strong>What is the PESA Act 1996?</strong> The Panchayats (Extension to Scheduled Areas) Act gives self-governance powers to Gram Sabhas in tribal areas.</li>
1492:               <li><strong>Name the first Chief Minister of Jharkhand.</strong> Babulal Marandi (took office on Nov 15, 2000).</li>
1493:             </ol>
1494:             <p><strong>Top 2 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1495:             <ul>
1496:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Trace the historical background and the socio-political movement for the creation of a separate Jharkhand state.</li>
1497:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Analyze the socio-economic impact of industrialization and the consequent rise of Left-Wing Extremism (Naxalism) in Jharkhand.</li>
1498:             </ul>
1499:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1500:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1501:               <p>For State Politics, know the timeline: Adivasi Mahasabha (1938) -> Jharkhand Party under Jaipal Singh Munda (1950) -> JMM (1973). Jharkhand was formed via Bihar Reorganisation Act 2000.</p>
1502:             </div>
1503:           </div>
1504: 
1505:           <!-- PAPER 3 (Political Sociology) -->
1506:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Political Sociology</h4>
1507:           <div class="content-box">
1508:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1509:             <ol>
1510:               <li><strong>Define Political Socialization.</strong> The lifelong process by which individuals learn and internalize political values and norms.</li>
1511:               <li><strong>What are the types of Political Culture?</strong> Almond and Verba identified three: Parochial, Subject, and Participant.</li>
1512:               <li><strong>What is the 'Iron Law of Oligarchy'?</strong> Robert Michels' theory that all organizations eventually become ruled by a small elite class.</li>
1513:               <li><strong>Define 'Circulation of Elites'.</strong> Vilfredo Pareto's concept that power shifts continuously between two types of elites: 'Lions' (force) and 'Foxes' (cunning).</li>
1514:               <li><strong>What is the role of family in political socialization?</strong> It is the primary and most influential agency that shapes an individual's early political orientation.</li>
1515:             </ol>
1516:             <p><strong>Top 2 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1517:             <ul>
1518:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Define Political Culture and critically examine its classification by Gabriel Almond and Sidney Verba.</li>
1519:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Critically examine the Elite Theory of Democracy with special reference to the contributions of Pareto, Mosca, and Michels.</li>
1520:             </ul>
1521:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1522:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1523:               <p>Key mapping: *The Civic Culture* (Almond & Verba). *The Ruling Class* (Mosca). *The Mind and Society* (Pareto). Elite theory fundamentally rejects Marxist class struggle.</p>
1524:             </div>
1525:           </div>
1526: 
1527:           <!-- PAPER 4 (Contemporary Political Issues) -->
1528:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Contemporary Political Issues</h4>
1529:           <div class="content-box">
1530:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1531:             <ol>
1532:               <li><strong>What is the 'North-South Divide'?</strong> The socio-economic disparity between the wealthy, developed Global North and the poorer, developing Global South.</li>
1533:               <li><strong>Define Sustainable Development.</strong> Development that meets present needs without compromising the ability of future generations to meet theirs (Brundtland Report, 1987).</li>
1534:               <li><strong>What does CBDR stand for?</strong> Common But Differentiated Responsibilities; recognizing that developed nations bear more historical responsibility for climate change.</li>
1535:               <li><strong>What is NIEO?</strong> New International Economic Order (1974); a set of proposals by developing countries to end economic colonialism and restructure global trade.</li>
1536:               <li><strong>Define Globalization.</strong> The increasing interconnectedness and interdependence of world economies, cultures, and populations.</li>
1537:             </ol>
1538:             <p><strong>Top 2 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1539:             <ul>
1540:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Analyze the demand for a New International Economic Order (NIEO) by developing countries. How relevant is it today?</li>
1541:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Discuss the concept of Sustainable Development. Critically evaluate the global efforts (like the Rio Summit and CBDR principle) to address climate change.</li>
1542:             </ul>
1543:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1544:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1545:               <p>Remember the Brandt Line (North-South divide). Brundtland Commission's report was titled "Our Common Future" (1987). NIEO was heavily championed by the Non-Aligned Movement (NAM).</p>
1546:             </div>

1558:           <h3 class="paper-title"><span class="hi">PSC-E-413A & 413B: अंतर्राष्ट्रीय संगठन एवं भारत की विदेश
1559:               नीति</span><span class="en">PSC-E-413A & 413B: International Organizations & India's Foreign Policy</span>
1560:           </h3>
1561: 
1562:           <h4 class="unit-title"><span class="hi">अंतर्राष्ट्रीय संगठन</span><span class="en">International
1563:               Organizations</span></h4>
1564:           <ul>
1565:             <li><strong><span class="hi">राष्ट्र संघ (League of Nations):</span><span class="en">League of
1566:                   Nations:</span></strong> <span class="hi">प्रथम विश्व युद्ध के बाद 1920 में स्थापित (वुडरो विल्सन के
1567:                 14 सूत्री कार्यक्रम का परिणाम)। यह द्वितीय विश्व युद्ध को रोकने में विफल रहा क्योंकि अमेरिका कभी इसमें
1568:                 शामिल नहीं हुआ और इसके पास अपनी कोई सेना नहीं थी।</span><span class="en">Established in 1920 after WWI
1569:                 (result of Woodrow Wilson's 14-point program). It failed to prevent WWII because the USA never joined
1570:                 and it lacked its own military force.</span></li>
1571:             <li><strong><span class="hi">संयुक्त राष्ट्र सुरक्षा परिषद (UNSC):</span><span class="en">UN Security
1572:                   Council (UNSC):</span></strong> <span class="hi">अंतर्राष्ट्रीय शांति और सुरक्षा के लिए जिम्मेदार।
1573:                 इसमें 15 सदस्य होते हैं: 5 स्थायी (P5 - जिनके पास वीटो पावर है) और 10 गैर-स्थायी (2 साल के कार्यकाल के
1574:                 लिए चुने गए)।</span><span class="en">Responsible for international peace and security. It has 15
1575:                 members: 5 permanent (P5 - with Veto power) and 10 non-permanent (elected for a 2-year term).</span>
1576:             </li>
1577:             <li><strong><span class="hi">रक्षा करने का उत्तरदायित्व (R2P - Responsibility to Protect):</span><span
1578:                   class="en">Responsibility to Protect (R2P):</span></strong> <span class="hi">2005 का UN सिद्धांत। यदि
1579:                 कोई राज्य अपनी आबादी को नरसंहार या युद्ध अपराधों से बचाने में विफल रहता है, तो अंतर्राष्ट्रीय समुदाय को
1580:                 हस्तक्षेप करने का अधिकार (और दायित्व) है।</span><span class="en">A 2005 UN principle. If a state fails
1581:                 to protect its population from genocide or war crimes, the international community has the right (and
1582:                 obligation) to intervene.</span></li>
1583:           </ul>
1584: 
1585:           <h4 class="unit-title"><span class="hi">भारत की विदेश नीति</span><span class="en">India's Foreign
1586:               Policy</span></h4>
1587:           <ul>
1588:             <li><strong><span class="hi">पंचशील (1954):</span><span class="en">Panchsheel (1954):</span></strong> <span
1589:                 class="hi">भारत और चीन के बीच शांतिपूर्ण सह-अस्तित्व के पांच सिद्धांत। 1. एक-दूसरे की क्षेत्रीय अखंडता
1590:                 का सम्मान, 2. गैर-आक्रामकता, 3. आंतरिक मामलों में गैर-हस्तक्षेप, 4. समानता और पारस्परिक लाभ, 5.
1591:                 शांतिपूर्ण सह-अस्तित्व।</span><span class="en">Five principles of peaceful coexistence between India and
1592:                 China. 1. Mutual respect for territorial integrity, 2. Non-aggression, 3. Non-interference in internal
1593:                 affairs, 4. Equality and mutual benefit, 5. Peaceful coexistence.</span></li>
1594:             <li><strong><span class="hi">लुक ईस्ट से एक्ट ईस्ट (Look East to Act East):</span><span class="en">Look East
1595:                   to Act East:</span></strong> <span class="hi">'लुक ईस्ट' नीति (1992 - नरसिम्हा राव) का उद्देश्य आसियान
1596:                 (ASEAN) देशों के साथ आर्थिक संबंध मजबूत करना था। 2014 में इसे 'एक्ट ईस्ट' नीति (PM मोदी) में अपग्रेड
1597:                 किया गया, जिसमें सामरिक और सुरक्षा सहयोग पर भी जोर दिया गया।</span><span class="en">'Look East' policy
1598:                 (1992 - Narasimha Rao) aimed to strengthen economic ties with ASEAN countries. Upgraded to 'Act East'
1599:                 policy in 2014 (PM Modi), emphasizing strategic and security cooperation as well.</span></li>
1600:             <li><strong><span class="hi">123 समझौता (2005-2008):</span><span class="en">123 Agreement
1601:                   (2005-2008):</span></strong> <span class="hi">भारत-अमेरिका असैन्य परमाणु समझौता। इसके तहत भारत अपनी
1602:                 सैन्य और असैन्य परमाणु सुविधाओं को अलग करने पर सहमत हुआ, और अमेरिका ने भारत को परमाणु ईंधन और तकनीक
1603:                 प्रदान की, भले ही भारत ने NPT (परमाणु अप्रसार संधि) पर हस्ताक्षर नहीं किए थे।</span><span
1604:                 class="en">Indo-US Civil Nuclear Agreement. India agreed to separate its military and civilian nuclear
1605:                 facilities, and the US provided nuclear fuel and technology, even though India hadn't signed the NPT
1606:                 (Non-Proliferation Treaty).</span></li>
1607:           </ul>
1608:         </div>
1609: 
1610:         <!-- Paper 414 -->
1611:         <div class="paper-section">
1612:           <h3 class="paper-title"><span class="hi">PSC-E-414A: अंतर्राष्ट्रीय कानून</span><span class="en">PSC-E-414A:
1613:               International Law</span></h3>
1614:           <p><strong><span class="hi">ह्यूगो ग्रोटियस (Hugo Grotius):</span><span class="en">Hugo
1615:                 Grotius:</span></strong> <span class="hi">इन्हें 'अंतर्राष्ट्रीय कानून का जनक' माना जाता है। उनकी
1616:               प्रसिद्ध पुस्तक 'डी ज्यूर बेली एक पैसिस' (युद्ध और शांति के कानून पर, 1625) है।</span><span
1617:               class="en">Considered the 'Father of International Law'. His famous book is 'De Jure Belli ac Pacis' (On
1618:               the Law of War and Peace, 1625).</span></p>
1619:           <div class="info-box">
1620:             <h4><span class="hi">अंतर्राष्ट्रीय कानून के स्रोत (ICJ के अनुच्छेद 38 के अनुसार)</span><span
1621:                 class="en">Sources of International Law (According to Article 38 of ICJ)</span></h4>
1622:             <ol>
1623:               <li><span class="hi">अंतर्राष्ट्रीय संधियाँ / कन्वेंशन (Treaties/Conventions)</span><span
1624:                   class="en">International Treaties / Conventions</span></li>
1625:               <li><span class="hi">अंतर्राष्ट्रीय प्रथा (Customs) — कानून के रूप में स्वीकृत सामान्य व्यवहार</span><span
1626:                   class="en">International Customs — general practice accepted as law</span></li>
1627:               <li><span class="hi">कानून के सामान्य सिद्धांत (General principles of law recognized by civilized
1628:                   nations)</span><span class="en">General principles of law recognized by civilized nations</span></li>
1629:               <li><span class="hi">न्यायिक निर्णय और न्यायविदों की शिक्षाएँ (Judicial decisions and teachings of highly
1630:                   qualified publicists)</span><span class="en">Judicial decisions and teachings of highly qualified
1631:                   publicists</span></li>
1632:             </ol>
1633:           </div>
1634:           <ul>
1635:             <li><strong><span class="hi">Pacta Sunt Servanda:</span><span class="en">Pacta Sunt
1636:                   Servanda:</span></strong> <span class="hi">अंतर्राष्ट्रीय कानून का एक मौलिक सिद्धांत जिसका अर्थ है
1637:                 "सहमति का पालन किया जाना चाहिए" (Agreements must be kept)।</span><span class="en">A fundamental
1638:                 principle of international law meaning "Agreements must be kept" (Treaties are binding upon the
1639:                 parties).</span></li>
1640:             <li><strong><span class="hi">प्रत्यर्पण (Extradition):</span><span class="en">Extradition:</span></strong>
1641:               <span class="hi">वह प्रक्रिया जिसके द्वारा एक राज्य, दूसरे राज्य के अनुरोध पर, किसी ऐसे व्यक्ति को सौंपता
1642:                 है जिस पर मुकदमा चलाने या सजा देने का आरोप है। राजनीतिक अपराधों के लिए आमतौर पर प्रत्यर्पण नहीं किया
1643:                 जाता है।</span><span class="en">The process by which one state, at the request of another, surrenders a
1644:                 person accused or convicted of a crime. Extradition is usually not granted for political
1645:                 offenses.</span></li>
1646:           </ul>
1647:         </div>
1648: 
1649:         <!-- Paper 415 -->
1650:         <div class="paper-section">
1651:           <h3 class="paper-title"><span class="hi">PSC-415 & 414C: तुलनात्मक सरकार एवं समकालीन मुद्दे</span><span
1652:               class="en">PSC-415 & 414C: Comparative Govt. & Contemporary Issues</span></h3>
1653:           <p><span class="hi">तुलनात्मक राजनीति में विभिन्न देशों की राजनीतिक प्रणालियों का अध्ययन किया जाता
1654:               है।</span><span class="en">Comparative politics involves the study of the political systems of different
1655:               countries.</span></p>
1656: 
1657:           <h4 class="unit-title"><span class="hi">विभिन्न राजनीतिक प्रणालियां</span><span class="en">Various Political
1658:               Systems</span></h4>
1659:           <ul>
1660:             <li><strong><span class="hi">USA (अध्यक्षीय प्रणाली - Presidential System):</span><span class="en">USA
1661:                   (Presidential System):</span></strong> <span class="hi">कार्यपालिका विधायिका से स्वतंत्र होती है।
1662:                 शक्तियों का सख्त पृथक्करण। राष्ट्रपति राज्य और सरकार दोनों का प्रमुख होता है।</span><span
1663:                 class="en">Executive is independent of the legislature. Strict separation of powers. President is both
1664:                 head of state and head of government.</span></li>
1665:             <li><strong><span class="hi">UK (संसदीय प्रणाली - Parliamentary System):</span><span class="en">UK
1666:                   (Parliamentary System):</span></strong> <span class="hi">संसदीय संप्रभुता (संसद कुछ भी कर सकती है)।
1667:                 कार्यपालिका विधायिका (संसद) से ली जाती है और उसी के प्रति उत्तरदायी होती है। वेस्टमिंस्टर
1668:                 मॉडल।</span><span class="en">Parliamentary sovereignty (Parliament can do anything). Executive is drawn
1669:                 from and responsible to the legislature (Parliament). Westminster model.</span></li>
1670:             <li><strong><span class="hi">फ्रांस (अर्ध-अध्यक्षीय प्रणाली - Semi-presidential System):</span><span
1671:                   class="en">France (Semi-presidential System):</span></strong> <span class="hi">एक शक्तिशाली प्रत्यक्ष
1672:                 निर्वाचित राष्ट्रपति और संसद के प्रति उत्तरदायी एक प्रधानमंत्री दोनों होते हैं (Dual
1673:                 executive)।</span><span class="en">Features both a powerful directly elected President and a Prime
1674:                 Minister accountable to parliament (Dual executive).</span></li>
1675:             <li><strong><span class="hi">स्विट्जरलैंड (बहुल कार्यपालिका - Plural Executive):</span><span
1676:                   class="en">Switzerland (Plural Executive):</span></strong> <span class="hi">संघीय परिषद (Federal
1677:                 Council) में 7 सदस्य होते हैं जो सामूहिक रूप से राज्य के प्रमुख के रूप में कार्य करते हैं। प्रत्यक्ष
1678:                 लोकतंत्र के लिए भी प्रसिद्ध है (जनमत संग्रह)।</span><span class="en">The Federal Council consists of 7
1679:                 members acting collectively as the head of state. Also famous for direct democracy (Referendums).</span>
1680:             </li>
1681:           </ul>
1682: 
1683:           <h4 class="unit-title"><span class="hi">भारतीय समकालीन मुद्दे</span><span class="en">Indian Contemporary
1684:               Issues</span></h4>
1685:           <ul>
1686:             <li><strong><span class="hi">अनुच्छेद 370 का निरसन (Abrogation of Art. 370):</span><span
1687:                   class="en">Abrogation of Art. 370:</span></strong> <span class="hi">5 अगस्त 2019 को, जम्मू-कश्मीर की
1688:                 विशेष स्थिति को रद्द कर दिया गया। J&K पुनर्गठन अधिनियम द्वारा इसे दो केंद्र शासित प्रदेशों (J&K और
1689:                 लद्दाख) में विभाजित किया गया।</span><span class="en">On 5 August 2019, the special status of Jammu and
1690:                 Kashmir was revoked. The J&K Reorganization Act divided it into two Union Territories (J&K and
1691:                 Ladakh).</span></li>
1692:             <li><strong><span class="hi">NOTA (उपरोक्त में से कोई नहीं):</span><span class="en">NOTA (None of the
1693:                   Above):</span></strong> <span class="hi">2013 में सुप्रीम कोर्ट (PUCL बनाम भारत संघ) के फैसले के बाद
1694:                 EVM में पेश किया गया। यह मतदाताओं को 'नकारात्मक वोट' देने का अधिकार देता है।</span><span
1695:                 class="en">Introduced in EVMs in 2013 following a Supreme Court judgment (PUCL vs UoI). It gives voters
1696:                 the right to register a 'negative vote'.</span></li>
1697:             <li><strong><span class="hi">103वां संविधान संशोधन (EWS आरक्षण):</span><span class="en">103rd Constitutional
1698:                   Amendment (EWS Quota):</span></strong> <span class="hi">आर्थिक रूप से कमजोर वर्गों (EWS - जो SC/ST/OBC
1699:                 आरक्षण के अंतर्गत नहीं आते) के लिए शिक्षा और सरकारी नौकरियों में 10% आरक्षण प्रदान करता है।</span><span
1700:                 class="en">Provides a 10% reservation in education and government jobs for Economically Weaker Sections

1707:           <h3 class="paper-title" style="background: linear-gradient(135deg, #10b981 0%, #059669 100%); color: white;">
1708:             <i class="fas fa-trophy"></i>
1709:             <span class="hi">सेमेस्टर IV - मास्टर Q&A और UGC NET टिप्स</span>
1710:             <span class="en">Semester IV - Master Q&A & UGC NET Tips</span>
1711:           </h3>
1712: 
1713:           <p class="intro-text">
1714:             <span class="hi">परीक्षा में सर्वोच्च अंक (Gold Medal) और JRF के लिए अति-महत्वपूर्ण प्रश्न।</span>

1718:           <!-- PAPER 1 (Intl Org & Foreign Policy) -->
1719:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">International Organizations & India's Foreign Policy</h4>
1720:           <div class="content-box">
1721:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1722:             <ol>
1723:               <li><strong>Why did the League of Nations fail?</strong> The USA never joined; it lacked an independent military force; major powers (Japan, Italy, Germany) left it unchallenged.</li>
1724:               <li><strong>What is the Veto Power?</strong> The power of any of the 5 permanent members (P5: USA, UK, France, Russia, China) to block any UNSC substantive resolution.</li>
1725:               <li><strong>What is R2P?</strong> Responsibility to Protect (2005); the international community's duty to intervene when a state fails to protect its citizens from genocide or war crimes.</li>
1726:               <li><strong>What is Panchsheel (1954)?</strong> Five principles of peaceful co-existence agreed between India and China: mutual territorial respect, non-aggression, non-interference, equality, and peaceful co-existence.</li>
1727:               <li><strong>What is the 'Act East' Policy?</strong> An upgrade of India's 'Look East' policy (1992) by PM Modi in 2014, adding strategic and security dimensions to the economic engagement with ASEAN/East Asia.</li>
1728:             </ol>
1729:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1730:             <ul>
1731:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Critically examine the role and relevance of the UN Security Council in the 21st century. Discuss the case for its reform.</li>
1732:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Analyze the evolution of India's foreign policy from the Nehruvian era to the present.</li>
1733:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Evaluate India's nuclear doctrine and the significance of the Indo-US Civil Nuclear Agreement (123 Agreement).</li>
1734:             </ul>
1735:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1736:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1737:               <p>Know the P5: USA, UK, France, Russia, China. India seeks permanent membership. Remember India's Nuclear tests: Smiling Buddha (1974, Pokhran-I) and Shakti (1998, Pokhran-II).</p>
1738:             </div>
1739:           </div>
1740: 
1741:           <!-- PAPER 2 (International Law) -->
1742:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">International Law</h4>
1743:           <div class="content-box">
1744:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1745:             <ol>
1746:               <li><strong>Who is the 'Father of International Law'?</strong> Hugo Grotius, author of 'De Jure Belli ac Pacis' (1625).</li>
1747:               <li><strong>What are the sources of International Law?</strong> Per ICJ Art 38: Treaties, Customs, General principles, Judicial decisions, and Teachings of publicists.</li>
1748:               <li><strong>Define 'Pacta Sunt Servanda'.</strong> A foundational legal principle meaning "agreements must be kept"; treaties are binding upon parties.</li>
1749:               <li><strong>What is Extradition?</strong> The surrender of an accused/convicted person by one state to another for trial or punishment. Political offenses are generally exempt.</li>
1750:               <li><strong>What is the ICJ?</strong> The International Court of Justice, the principal judicial organ of the UN, located at The Hague. Only states (not individuals) can be parties before it.</li>
1751:             </ol>
1752:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1753:             <ul>
1754:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Discuss the sources of International Law as enumerated in Article 38 of the ICJ Statute.</li>
1755:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Explain the concept of State Sovereignty and discuss the challenges to it in the age of globalization and R2P.</li>
1756:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Analyze the role of the International Court of Justice (ICJ) and its limitations.</li>
1757:             </ul>
1758:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1759:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1760:               <p>ICJ vs ICC: ICJ settles disputes between states. ICC (International Criminal Court, est. 2002 Rome Statute) prosecutes individuals for genocide and war crimes. India has NOT ratified the ICC Rome Statute.</p>
1761:             </div>
1762:           </div>
1763: 
1764:           <!-- PAPER 3 (Comparative Govt & Contemporary Issues) -->
1765:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Comparative Govt. & Contemporary Issues</h4>
1766:           <div class="content-box">
1767:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1768:             <ol>
1769:               <li><strong>Differentiate Presidential and Parliamentary systems.</strong> Presidential (USA): Executive independent of legislature. Parliamentary (UK): Executive derived from and responsible to the legislature.</li>
1770:               <li><strong>What is 'Parliamentary Sovereignty'?</strong> The UK doctrine that Parliament is the supreme legal authority and can create or end any law, and no body can override or set aside its legislation.</li>
1771:               <li><strong>What is the French Semi-Presidential System?</strong> A 'dual executive' system with a powerful directly elected President and a Prime Minister responsible to the National Assembly.</li>
1772:               <li><strong>What is the Swiss Plural Executive?</strong> A 7-member Federal Council acts collectively as the head of state. No single person holds supreme executive power.</li>
1773:               <li><strong>What is the significance of Abrogation of Article 370?</strong> In August 2019, the special status of J&K was revoked, and the state was bifurcated into two Union Territories.</li>
1774:             </ol>
1775:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1776:             <ul>
1777:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Compare and contrast the Presidential system (USA) and the Parliamentary system (UK).</li>
1778:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Discuss the significance and implications of the abrogation of Article 370 for Indian federalism.</li>
1779:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Evaluate the 103rd Constitutional Amendment (EWS Quota). Does it violate the Basic Structure?</li>
1780:             </ul>
1781:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1782:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1783:               <p>Key constitutional systems: USA = Separation of Powers + Judicial Review. UK = Parliamentary Sovereignty + Rule of Law (Dicey). France = Semi-Presidential (5th Republic, 1958). Switzerland = Direct Democracy (Referendums).</p>
1784:             </div>
1785:           </div>
1786:         </div>
1787:       </div>

868:           <!-- PAPER 1 (FC-101 / PSC-F-101) -->
869:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Political Theory (राजनीतिक सिद्धांत)</h4>
870:           <div class="content-box">
871:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
872:             <ol>
873:               <li><strong>What is the 'Post-Behavioral Revolution'?</strong> Led by David Easton, focusing on 'Action' and 'Relevance' to solve real-world problems.</li>
874:               <li><strong>Explain John Rawls' 'Veil of Ignorance'.</strong> A thought experiment where individuals design a just society without knowing their status.</li>
875:               <li><strong>Define 'Negative Liberty'.</strong> The absence of external constraints (Hobbes, Berlin).</li>
876:               <li><strong>What is 'Multiculturalism'?</strong> A political philosophy that accommodates cultural differences of minority groups.</li>
877:               <li><strong>What is 'Hegemony' (Gramsci)?</strong> Ideological domination of the ruling class through manufactured consent.</li>
878:             </ol>
879:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
880:             <ul>
881:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Examine the debate on the 'Decline and Resurgence' of Political Theory. (Focus: Easton, Laslett, Rawls).</li>
882:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Critically analyze John Rawls' Theory of Justice. (Focus: Two Principles, Difference Principle).</li>
883:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Compare Negative and Positive Liberty with reference to Isaiah Berlin.</li>
884:             </ul>
885:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
886:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
887:               <p>Memorize Isaiah Berlin's 1958 essay "Two Concepts of Liberty". Know Peter Laslett's quote: "Political philosophy is dead."</p>
888:             </div>
889:           </div>
890: 
891:           <!-- PAPER 2 (CC-102 / PSC-C-103) -->
892:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Western Political Thought (पाश्चात्य राजनीतिक विचार)</h4>
893:           <div class="content-box">
894:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
895:             <ol>
896:               <li><strong>What is Plato's concept of 'Philosopher King'?</strong> A ruler with true knowledge, free from family/property ties.</li>
897:               <li><strong>Define Aristotle's 'Distributive Justice'.</strong> Distribution of offices according to merit (geometric proportion).</li>
898:               <li><strong>What is Hobbes' 'State of Nature'?</strong> "War of every man against every man"; life is solitary, poor, nasty, brutish, and short.</li>
899:               <li><strong>What is J.S. Mill's 'Harm Principle'?</strong> State interference is only justified to prevent harm to others.</li>
900:               <li><strong>Define Marx's 'Historical Materialism'.</strong> Material conditions (base) determine the social and political structure (superstructure).</li>
901:             </ol>
902:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
903:             <ul>
904:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Compare and contrast the Social Contract theories of Hobbes, Locke, and Rousseau.</li>
905:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Analyze Karl Marx's critique of Capitalism and his vision of a Communist society.</li>
906:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Evaluate Rousseau's paradox: "Man is forced to be free."</li>
907:             </ul>
908:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
909:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
910:               <p>Chronology is King! Arrange Plato's books (Republic, Statesman, Laws) in order. Understand the difference between Hegel's Dialectical Idealism and Marx's Dialectical Materialism.</p>
911:             </div>
912:           </div>
913: 
914:           <!-- PAPER 3 (CC-103 / PSC-C-102) -->
915:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Indian Political Thought (भारतीय राजनीतिक विचार)</h4>
916:           <div class="content-box">
917:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
918:             <ol>
919:               <li><strong>Explain Kautilya's concept of 'Amatya'.</strong> High-ranking officials/ministers in the Saptanga theory.</li>
920:               <li><strong>What is the 'Drain Theory'?</strong> Dadabhai Naoroji's theory that British rule systematically drained India's wealth.</li>
921:               <li><strong>Define Gandhi's 'Trusteeship'.</strong> Wealthy individuals act as 'trustees', using surplus for societal welfare.</li>
922:               <li><strong>What is 'Radical Humanism'?</strong> M.N. Roy's philosophy focusing on individual reason and freedom, rejecting Marxism.</li>
923:               <li><strong>What is 'Annihilation of Caste'?</strong> B.R. Ambedkar's call to destroy the caste system and its religious texts.</li>
924:             </ol>
925:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
926:             <ul>
927:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Critically examine Kautilya's Saptanga Theory of State and Mandala Theory.</li>
928:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Evaluate the debate between Gandhi and Ambedkar on the issue of Caste and Untouchability.</li>
929:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Analyze the political philosophy of Bal Gangadhar Tilak (Swaraj, Nationalism).</li>
930:             </ul>

934:             </div>

944:               <li><strong>What is 'Political Culture'?</strong> Almond and Verba's concept (Parochial, Subject, Participant cultures).</li>

1193:               <div class="qa-content">
1194:                 <h5>1. Introduction</h5>
1195:                 <p>Bal Gangadhar Tilak, known as the "Father of Indian Unrest," shifted the Indian national movement from the petition-politics of Moderates to mass-based radical nationalism.</p>
1196:                 <h5>2. Concept of Swaraj</h5>
1197:                 <ul>
1198:                   <li>Tilak famously declared, <em>"Swaraj is my birthright, and I shall have it."</em></li>
1199:                   <li>For him, Swaraj was not just political freedom (home rule) but a Dharma (moral duty). It meant Indian control over Indian affairs, rejecting British cultural and political hegemony.</li>
1200:                 </ul>
1201:                 <h5>3. Cultural Nationalism</h5>
1202:                 <ul>
1203:                   <li>Unlike early moderates who admired Western institutions, Tilak rooted his nationalism in Indian culture and Hindu traditions.</li>
1204:                   <li>He revitalized public festivals—the <strong>Ganapati festival</strong> (1893) and the <strong>Shivaji festival</strong> (1895)—using them to mobilize the masses politically and foster a sense of unity.</li>
1205:                 </ul>
1206:                 <h5>4. Methods of Struggle</h5>
1207:                 <p>He advocated the four-point program: <strong>Boycott, Swadeshi, National Education, and Passive Resistance</strong>. He popularized these through his newspapers, <em>Kesari</em> (Marathi) and <em>Mahratta</em> (English).</p>
1208:                 <h5>5. Conclusion</h5>
1209:                 <p>Tilak democratized the freedom struggle, linking political emancipation with cultural pride, laying the groundwork for Gandhi's later mass movements.</p>
1210:               </div>
1211:             </details>

1219:           <!-- PAPER 4 (CC-104 / PSC-C-104) -->
1220:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;"><i class="fas fa-globe"></i> Comparative Politics (तुलनात्मक राजनीति)</h4>
1221:           <div class="content-box">
1222:             <h5 class="qa-section-title"><i class="fas fa-bolt" style="color: #f59e0b;"></i> Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</h5>
1223: 
1224:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1225:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q1</span> Define David Easton's 'Input-Output Model'.</summary>
1226:               <div class="qa-content">
1227:                 <p>A systems approach to politics where the political system operates in an environment. Citizens provide <strong>Inputs</strong> (Demands like lower taxes, and Supports like voting). The political system (government) processes these and produces <strong>Outputs</strong> (Laws, policies). Feedback loops connect outputs back to new inputs.</p>
1228:               </div>
1229:             </details>
1230: 
1231:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1232:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q2</span> What is 'Interest Articulation'?</summary>
1233:               <div class="qa-content">
1234:                 <p>In Almond's structural-functional framework, it is the process by which individuals and groups express their demands and grievances to political decision-makers. It is primarily performed by <strong>Pressure Groups</strong> and NGOs.</p>
1235:               </div>
1236:             </details>
1237: 
1238:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1239:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q3</span> What is 'Political Culture'?</summary>
1240:               <div class="qa-content">
1241:                 <p>Defined by Gabriel Almond and Sidney Verba in <em>'The Civic Culture'</em>, it is the set of attitudes, beliefs, and sentiments that give order and meaning to a political process. They classified it into Parochial (unaware), Subject (aware but inactive), and Participant (active).</p>
1242:               </div>
1243:             </details>
1244: 
1245:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1246:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q4</span> Differentiate Federal and Unitary systems.</summary>
1247:               <div class="qa-content">
1248:                 <p><strong>Federal:</strong> Power is constitutionally divided between a central government and regional units (e.g., USA, India). <br><strong>Unitary:</strong> All supreme power is concentrated in a single central government; regional units only have delegated powers (e.g., UK, France).</p>
1249:               </div>
1250:             </details>
1251: 
1252:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1253:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q5</span> Explain 'Rule of Law'.</summary>
1254:               <div class="qa-content">
1255:                 <p>A concept popularized by A.V. Dicey, meaning that <strong>no one is above the law</strong>. It entails the absolute supremacy of regular law as opposed to arbitrary power, equality before the law, and the protection of individual rights.</p>
1256:               </div>
1257:             </details>
1258: 
1259:             <h5 class="qa-section-title" style="margin-top: 20px;"><i class="fas fa-pen-nib" style="color: #3b82f6;"></i> Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</h5>
1260: 
1261:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1262:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q1</span> Critically examine the Structural-Functional approach of Gabriel Almond. <span class="qa-marks">[20 Marks]</span></summary>
1263:               <div class="qa-content">
1264:                 <h5>1. Introduction</h5>
1265:                 <p>Gabriel Almond developed the Structural-Functional approach as a tool for comparing different political systems (especially developed and developing nations) by looking at what functions they perform, rather than just their formal institutions.</p>
1266:                 <h5>2. Core Premise</h5>
1267:                 <p>Every political system has certain structures (institutions like parties, courts) that perform specific functions. To understand a system, we must ask: "What structures perform what functions?"</p>
1268:                 <h5>3. Input Functions (Performed by society/non-state actors)</h5>
1269:                 <ul>
1270:                   <li><strong>Political Socialization & Recruitment:</strong> Inducting people into political roles (Family, Schools).</li>
1271:                   <li><strong>Interest Articulation:</strong> Expressing demands (Pressure Groups).</li>
1272:                   <li><strong>Interest Aggregation:</strong> Combining demands into policy alternatives (Political Parties).</li>
1273:                   <li><strong>Political Communication:</strong> Flow of information (Media).</li>
1274:                 </ul>
1275:                 <h5>4. Output Functions (Performed by the state)</h5>
1276:                 <ul>
1277:                   <li><strong>Rule-making:</strong> Making laws (Legislature).</li>
1278:                   <li><strong>Rule-application:</strong> Implementing laws (Executive/Bureaucracy).</li>
1279:                   <li><strong>Rule-adjudication:</strong> Resolving disputes (Judiciary).</li>
1280:                 </ul>
1281:                 <h5>5. Criticism</h5>
1282:                 <p>Critics argue it suffers from a Western bias (ethnocentrism), assuming the Anglo-American democratic model is the ideal. It is also criticized for focusing too much on systemic stability and ignoring revolutionary change.</p>
1283:               </div>
1284:             </details>
1285: 
1286:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1287:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q2</span> Discuss the theories of Political Development formulated by Lucian Pye and Samuel Huntington. <span class="qa-marks">[20 Marks]</span></summary>
1288:               <div class="qa-content">
1289:                 <h5>1. Introduction</h5>
1290:                 <p>In the 1960s, political scientists sought to understand how newly independent nations of the "Third World" modernize politically. Pye and Huntington provided the most influential frameworks.</p>
1291:                 <h5>2. Lucian Pye's Development Syndrome</h5>
1292:                 <p>Pye identified three core characteristics of political development (the "Development Syndrome"):</p>
1293:                 <ul>
1294:                   <li><strong>Equality:</strong> Mass participation, universal laws, and recruitment based on achievement rather than birth.</li>
1295:                   <li><strong>Capacity:</strong> The government's ability to manage public affairs, enforce laws, and manage tensions effectively.</li>
1296:                   <li><strong>Differentiation:</strong> Specialization of political roles and structures (e.g., separation of judiciary and executive).</li>
1297:                 </ul>
1298:                 <h5>3. Samuel Huntington's Institutionalization Theory</h5>
1299:                 <p>Huntington challenged the optimistic view that economic modernization naturally leads to political development. In <em>'Political Order in Changing Societies'</em>, he argued:</p>
1300:                 <ul>

1300:                 <ul>
1301:                   <li>Rapid social mobilization without adequate political institutions leads to <strong>Political Decay</strong> (chaos, coups, instability).</li>
1302:                   <li>Political development is defined as the <strong>institutionalization</strong> of political organizations and procedures (adaptability, complexity, autonomy, coherence).</li>
1303:                   <li>Order must precede democracy in developing nations.</li>
1304:                 </ul>
1305:                 <h5>4. Conclusion</h5>
1306:                 <p>While Pye focused on the qualitative characteristics of a developed polity, Huntington focused on the painful process of achieving stability, making his theory highly relevant for analyzing modern fragile states.</p>
1307:               </div>
1308:             </details>
1309: 
1310:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1311:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q3</span> Compare the Presidential system of the USA with the Parliamentary system of the UK. <span class="qa-marks">[15 Marks]</span></summary>
1312:               <div class="qa-content">
1313:                 <h5>1. Introduction</h5>
1314:                 <p>The USA and UK represent the two classic democratic models, differing fundamentally in the relationship between the executive and legislative branches.</p>
1315:                 <h5>2. Separation of Powers vs. Fusion of Powers</h5>
1316:                 <ul>
1317:                   <li><strong>USA (Presidential):</strong> Strict Separation of Powers. The President (Executive) is elected separately from Congress (Legislature). They have separate tenures and cannot be members of each other's branches.</li>
1318:                   <li><strong>UK (Parliamentary):</strong> Fusion of Powers. The Prime Minister and Cabinet are drawn from the Parliament (Legislature) and sit in it.</li>
1319:                 </ul>
1320:                 <h5>3. Head of State and Government</h5>
1321:                 <ul>
1322:                   <li><strong>USA:</strong> The President is both the ceremonial Head of State and the actual Head of Government.</li>
1323:                   <li><strong>UK:</strong> The Monarch is the ceremonial Head of State, while the Prime Minister is the real Head of Government.</li>
1324:                 </ul>
1325:                 <h5>4. Accountability and Tenure</h5>
1326:                 <ul>
1327:                   <li><strong>USA:</strong> The President serves a fixed 4-year term and cannot be removed by Congress on a vote of no-confidence (only via difficult impeachment for crimes).</li>
1328:                   <li><strong>UK:</strong> The Prime Minister relies on the continuous support of the Parliament. A 'Vote of No Confidence' can remove the government immediately.</li>
1329:                 </ul>
1330:                 <h5>5. Conclusion</h5>
1331:                 <p>The US system prioritizes checks and balances and stability, sometimes leading to gridlock. The UK system prioritizes efficiency and accountability, but can lead to "elective dictatorship" if the majority is large.</p>
1332:               </div>
1333:             </details>
1334: 
1335:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1336:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1337:               <p>Memorize the 5 countries in 'The Civic Culture' (USA, UK, Germany, Italy, Mexico). Match Almond's structures correctly (Interest Articulation = Pressure Groups).</p>
1338:             </div>
1339:           </div>

1355:           <!-- PAPER 1 (Academic Writing) -->
1356:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Academic Writing and Communication Skills</h4>
1357:           <div class="content-box">
1358:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1359:             <ol>
1360:               <li><strong>What is a Research Synopsis?</strong> A blueprint or summary of proposed research detailing the problem, objectives, and methodology.</li>
1361:               <li><strong>What does APA stand for and where is it used?</strong> American Psychological Association; used primarily in Social Sciences.</li>
1362:               <li><strong>Explain the 'Author-Date' citation system.</strong> In-text citations include the author's last name and publication year, e.g., (Smith, 2020).</li>
1363:               <li><strong>What is Plagiarism?</strong> The unethical practice of presenting someone else's work or ideas as your own without proper acknowledgment.</li>
1364:               <li><strong>What is a Literature Review?</strong> A critical analysis of existing published research relevant to your topic.</li>
1365:             </ol>
1366:             <p><strong>Top 2 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1367:             <ul>
1368:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Define Academic Writing and discuss its key characteristics compared to creative writing.</li>
1369:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Explain the different standard Citation Styles (APA, MLA, Chicago). Why is proper citation essential in research?</li>
1370:             </ul>
1371:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1372:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1373:               <p>For Research Aptitude (Paper 1), remember: APA is Author-Date (Social Sciences). MLA is Author-Page (Humanities). Chicago uses Footnotes/Endnotes (History).</p>
1374:             </div>
1375:           </div>
