1377:           <!-- PAPER 2 (International Relations) -->
1378:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Theories of International Politics</h4>
1379:           <div class="content-box">
1380:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1381:             <ol>
1382:               <li><strong>What is 'Classical Realism'?</strong> Hans Morgenthau's theory that states act out of a natural human desire for power.</li>
1383:               <li><strong>What is 'Neo-Realism'?</strong> Kenneth Waltz's theory that the anarchic structure of the international system, not human nature, dictates state behavior.</li>
1384:               <li><strong>Define 'Balance of Power'.</strong> A mechanism where states form alliances to prevent any single state from becoming dominant.</li>
1385:               <li><strong>What is 'Collective Security'?</strong> An arrangement (like the UN) where an attack on one state is treated as an attack on all.</li>
1386:               <li><strong>What is the core argument of Constructivism?</strong> Alexander Wendt argued that "Anarchy is what states make of it"—international relations are socially constructed by ideas and norms.</li>
1387:             </ol>
1388:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1389:             <ul>
1390:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Critically examine Hans Morgenthau’s Six Principles of Political Realism.</li>
1391:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Differentiate between Classical Realism (Morgenthau) and Structural Realism (Waltz).</li>
1392:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Analyze the relevance of the Non-Aligned Movement (NAM) in the contemporary multi-polar world.</li>
1393:             </ul>
1394:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1395:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1396:               <p>Match the book to the thinker: *Politics Among Nations* (Morgenthau), *Theory of International Politics* (Waltz), *The Tragedy of Great Power Politics* (Mearsheimer - Offensive Realism).</p>
1397:             </div>
1398:           </div>
1399: 
1400:           <!-- PAPER 3 (Public Administration) -->
1401:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Public Administration</h4>
1402:           <div class="content-box">
1403:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1404:             <ol>
1405:               <li><strong>What is the 'Hawthorne Effect'?</strong> Elton Mayo's finding that workers' productivity improves when they feel observed and valued.</li>
1406:               <li><strong>Define 'Bounded Rationality'.</strong> Herbert Simon's concept that decision-makers lack complete information and cognitive ability, so they "satisfice" instead of "optimize".</li>
1407:               <li><strong>What are the features of Weber's Ideal Bureaucracy?</strong> Hierarchy, formal rules, specialization, impersonality, and merit-based selection.</li>
1408:               <li><strong>What is the 'Prismatic-Sala' model?</strong> F.W. Riggs' model explaining administration in developing societies characterized by Formalism, Heterogeneity, and Overlapping.</li>
1409:               <li><strong>Define 'Zero-Based Budgeting' (ZBB).</strong> A budgeting method requiring every expense to be justified from 'scratch' (zero) each year.</li>
1410:             </ol>
1411:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1412:             <ul>
1413:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Evaluate Herbert Simon's Decision-Making Approach in Public Administration.</li>
1414:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Critically analyze Max Weber’s theory of Bureaucracy. Discuss Robert Merton's critique of it.</li>
1415:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Examine the concept, evolution, and core principles of New Public Administration (NPA).</li>
1416:             </ul>
1417:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1418:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1419:               <p>Keywords mapping: "Satisficing" = Simon. "Prismatic/Sala" = Riggs. "Scientific Management" = Taylor. "Social Equity/Minnowbrook" = NPA (Frederickson).</p>
1420:             </div>
1421:           </div>
1422: 
1423:           <!-- PAPER 4 (Western Political Thought / Indian Political System) -->
1424:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Indian Political System & Western Thought</h4>
1425:           <div class="content-box">
1426:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1427:             <ol>
1428:               <li><strong>What is the 'Basic Structure Doctrine'?</strong> Established in Kesavananda Bharati (1973), it prevents Parliament from altering the fundamental features of the Constitution.</li>
1429:               <li><strong>Define 'Judicial Activism'.</strong> The judiciary playing a proactive role to protect citizen rights (e.g., through PILs).</li>
1430:               <li><strong>What is Aristotle's classification of the State?</strong> He classified states by the number of rulers and their intent (Rule of One: Monarchy/Tyranny; Rule of Few: Aristocracy/Oligarchy; Rule of Many: Polity/Democracy).</li>
1431:               <li><strong>What is J.S. Mill's 'Harm Principle'?</strong> State intervention is only justified to prevent an individual from harming others.</li>
1432:               <li><strong>What is Marx's 'Historical Materialism'?</strong> The theory that economic structures (the base) shape all political and social institutions (the superstructure).</li>
1433:             </ol>
1434:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1435:             <ul>
1436:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> "The Indian Constitution is federal in form but unitary in spirit." Discuss.</li>
1437:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Analyze Machiavelli's advice to a ruler as outlined in 'The Prince'. Why is he considered the first modern political thinker?</li>
1438:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Discuss Karl Marx's theory of Class Struggle and Surplus Value.</li>
1439:             </ul>
1440:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1441:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1442:               <p>For Indian Polity, remember Art 32 (5 Writs), Art 143 (Advisory Jurisdiction), Art 356 (President's Rule). For Western Thought, remember Machiavelli separated Politics from Ethics/Religion.</p>
1443:             </div>
1444:           </div>

1963:           <!-- PAPER 1 (Human Rights) -->
1964:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Human Rights</h4>
1965:           <div class="content-box">
1966:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1967:             <ol>
1968:               <li><strong>What are the three generations of human rights?</strong> Karel Vasak classified them as Civil/Political (1st), Economic/Social (2nd), and Collective/Solidarity (3rd) rights.</li>
1969:               <li><strong>What is the UDHR?</strong> The Universal Declaration of Human Rights, adopted by the UN General Assembly on Dec 10, 1948.</li>
1970:               <li><strong>Difference between ICCPR and ICESCR?</strong> ICCPR covers civil/political rights (negative rights). ICESCR covers economic/social/cultural rights (positive rights requiring state action).</li>
1971:               <li><strong>What is the NHRC?</strong> The National Human Rights Commission (India), a statutory body established in 1993 to protect and promote human rights.</li>
1972:               <li><strong>Define 'inalienable rights'.</strong> Rights that cannot be taken away, given away, or transferred, as they are inherent to all human beings.</li>
1973:             </ol>
1974:             <p><strong>Top 2 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1975:             <ul>
1976:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Discuss the historical evolution of Human Rights with reference to the three generations proposed by Karel Vasak.</li>
1977:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Critically examine the Universal Declaration of Human Rights (UDHR) 1948 and its impact on global politics.</li>
1978:             </ul>
1979:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
1980:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
1981:               <p>Dates matter: Human Rights Day is Dec 10. NHRC established in 1993. Know that 1st generation rights correlate to "Liberty", 2nd to "Equality", and 3rd to "Fraternity".</p>
1982:             </div>
1983:           </div>

1985:           <!-- PAPER 2 (Jharkhand Politics) -->
1986:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Jharkhand Politics</h4>
1987:           <div class="content-box">
1988:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
1989:             <ol>
1990:               <li><strong>What was the Birsa Munda 'Ulgulan'?</strong> The Great Rebellion (1899-1900) by Birsa Munda against British agrarian policies and non-tribal landlords.</li>
1991:               <li><strong>What is the CNT Act 1908?</strong> The Chota Nagpur Tenancy Act restricts the transfer of tribal land to non-tribals to prevent exploitation.</li>
1992:               <li><strong>Define the 'Resource Curse' in Jharkhand.</strong> The paradox where Jharkhand has massive mineral wealth but suffers from extreme poverty and underdevelopment.</li>
1993:               <li><strong>What is the PESA Act 1996?</strong> The Panchayats (Extension to Scheduled Areas) Act gives self-governance powers to Gram Sabhas in tribal areas.</li>
1994:               <li><strong>Name the first Chief Minister of Jharkhand.</strong> Babulal Marandi (took office on Nov 15, 2000).</li>
1995:             </ol>
1996:             <p><strong>Top 2 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
1997:             <ul>
1998:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Trace the historical background and the socio-political movement for the creation of a separate Jharkhand state.</li>
1999:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Analyze the socio-economic impact of industrialization and the consequent rise of Left-Wing Extremism (Naxalism) in Jharkhand.</li>
2000:             </ul>
2001:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
2002:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
2003:               <p>For State Politics, know the timeline: Adivasi Mahasabha (1938) -> Jharkhand Party under Jaipal Singh Munda (1950) -> JMM (1973). Jharkhand was formed via Bihar Reorganisation Act 2000.</p>

2007:           <!-- PAPER 3 (Political Sociology) -->
2008:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Political Sociology</h4>
2009:           <div class="content-box">
2010:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
2011:             <ol>
2012:               <li><strong>Define Political Socialization.</strong> The lifelong process by which individuals learn and internalize political values and norms.</li>
2013:               <li><strong>What are the types of Political Culture?</strong> Almond and Verba identified three: Parochial, Subject, and Participant.</li>
2014:               <li><strong>What is the 'Iron Law of Oligarchy'?</strong> Robert Michels' theory that all organizations eventually become ruled by a small elite class.</li>
2015:               <li><strong>Define 'Circulation of Elites'.</strong> Vilfredo Pareto's concept that power shifts continuously between two types of elites: 'Lions' (force) and 'Foxes' (cunning).</li>
2016:               <li><strong>What is the role of family in political socialization?</strong> It is the primary and most influential agency that shapes an individual's early political orientation.</li>
2017:             </ol>
2018:             <p><strong>Top 2 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
2019:             <ul>
2020:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Define Political Culture and critically examine its classification by Gabriel Almond and Sidney Verba.</li>
2021:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Critically examine the Elite Theory of Democracy with special reference to the contributions of Pareto, Mosca, and Michels.</li>
2022:             </ul>
2023:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
2024:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
2025:               <p>Key mapping: *The Civic Culture* (Almond & Verba). *The Ruling Class* (Mosca). *The Mind and Society* (Pareto). Elite theory fundamentally rejects Marxist class struggle.</p>
2026:             </div>
2027:           </div>

2029:           <!-- PAPER 4 (Contemporary Political Issues) -->
2030:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Contemporary Political Issues</h4>
2031:           <div class="content-box">
2032:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
2033:             <ol>
2034:               <li><strong>What is the 'North-South Divide'?</strong> The socio-economic disparity between the wealthy, developed Global North and the poorer, developing Global South.</li>
2035:               <li><strong>Define Sustainable Development.</strong> Development that meets present needs without compromising the ability of future generations to meet theirs (Brundtland Report, 1987).</li>
2036:               <li><strong>What does CBDR stand for?</strong> Common But Differentiated Responsibilities; recognizing that developed nations bear more historical responsibility for climate change.</li>
2037:               <li><strong>What is NIEO?</strong> New International Economic Order (1974); a set of proposals by developing countries to end economic colonialism and restructure global trade.</li>
2038:               <li><strong>Define Globalization.</strong> The increasing interconnectedness and interdependence of world economies, cultures, and populations.</li>
2039:             </ol>
2040:             <p><strong>Top 2 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
2041:             <ul>
2042:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Analyze the demand for a New International Economic Order (NIEO) by developing countries. How relevant is it today?</li>
2043:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Discuss the concept of Sustainable Development. Critically evaluate the global efforts (like the Rio Summit and CBDR principle) to address climate change.</li>
2044:             </ul>
2045:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
2046:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
2047:               <p>Remember the Brandt Line (North-South divide). Brundtland Commission's report was titled "Our Common Future" (1987). NIEO was heavily championed by the Non-Aligned Movement (NAM).</p>

2509:           <!-- PAPER 1 (Intl Org & Foreign Policy) -->
2510:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">International Organizations & India's Foreign Policy</h4>
2511:           <div class="content-box">
2512:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
2513:             <ol>
2514:               <li><strong>Why did the League of Nations fail?</strong> The USA never joined; it lacked an independent military force; major powers (Japan, Italy, Germany) left it unchallenged.</li>
2515:               <li><strong>What is the Veto Power?</strong> The power of any of the 5 permanent members (P5: USA, UK, France, Russia, China) to block any UNSC substantive resolution.</li>
2516:               <li><strong>What is R2P?</strong> Responsibility to Protect (2005); the international community's duty to intervene when a state fails to protect its citizens from genocide or war crimes.</li>
2517:               <li><strong>What is Panchsheel (1954)?</strong> Five principles of peaceful co-existence agreed between India and China: mutual territorial respect, non-aggression, non-interference, equality, and peaceful co-existence.</li>
2518:               <li><strong>What is the 'Act East' Policy?</strong> An upgrade of India's 'Look East' policy (1992) by PM Modi in 2014, adding strategic and security dimensions to the economic engagement with ASEAN/East Asia.</li>
2519:             </ol>
2520:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
2521:             <ul>
2522:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Critically examine the role and relevance of the UN Security Council in the 21st century. Discuss the case for its reform.</li>
2523:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Analyze the evolution of India's foreign policy from the Nehruvian era to the present.</li>
2524:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Evaluate India's nuclear doctrine and the significance of the Indo-US Civil Nuclear Agreement (123 Agreement).</li>
2525:             </ul>
2526:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
2527:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
2528:               <p>Know the P5: USA, UK, France, Russia, China. India seeks permanent membership. Remember India's Nuclear tests: Smiling Buddha (1974, Pokhran-I) and Shakti (1998, Pokhran-II).</p>
2529:             </div>
2530:           </div>
2531: 
2532:           <!-- PAPER 2 (International Law) -->
2533:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">International Law</h4>
2534:           <div class="content-box">
2535:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
2536:             <ol>
2537:               <li><strong>Who is the 'Father of International Law'?</strong> Hugo Grotius, author of 'De Jure Belli ac Pacis' (1625).</li>
2538:               <li><strong>What are the sources of International Law?</strong> Per ICJ Art 38: Treaties, Customs, General principles, Judicial decisions, and Teachings of publicists.</li>
2539:               <li><strong>Define 'Pacta Sunt Servanda'.</strong> A foundational legal principle meaning "agreements must be kept"; treaties are binding upon parties.</li>
2540:               <li><strong>What is Extradition?</strong> The surrender of an accused/convicted person by one state to another for trial or punishment. Political offenses are generally exempt.</li>
2541:               <li><strong>What is the ICJ?</strong> The International Court of Justice, the principal judicial organ of the UN, located at The Hague. Only states (not individuals) can be parties before it.</li>
2542:             </ol>
2543:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
2544:             <ul>
2545:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Discuss the sources of International Law as enumerated in Article 38 of the ICJ Statute.</li>
2546:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Explain the concept of State Sovereignty and discuss the challenges to it in the age of globalization and R2P.</li>
2547:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Analyze the role of the International Court of Justice (ICJ) and its limitations.</li>
2548:             </ul>
2549:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
2550:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
2551:               <p>ICJ vs ICC: ICJ settles disputes between states. ICC (International Criminal Court, est. 2002 Rome Statute) prosecutes individuals for genocide and war crimes. India has NOT ratified the ICC Rome Statute.</p>
2552:             </div>
2553:           </div>
2554: 
2555:           <!-- PAPER 3 (Comparative Govt & Contemporary Issues) -->
2556:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Comparative Govt. & Contemporary Issues</h4>
2557:           <div class="content-box">
2558:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
2559:             <ol>
2560:               <li><strong>Differentiate Presidential and Parliamentary systems.</strong> Presidential (USA): Executive independent of legislature. Parliamentary (UK): Executive derived from and responsible to the legislature.</li>
2561:               <li><strong>What is 'Parliamentary Sovereignty'?</strong> The UK doctrine that Parliament is the supreme legal authority and can create or end any law, and no body can override or set aside its legislation.</li>
2562:               <li><strong>What is the French Semi-Presidential System?</strong> A 'dual executive' system with a powerful directly elected President and a Prime Minister responsible to the National Assembly.</li>
2563:               <li><strong>What is the Swiss Plural Executive?</strong> A 7-member Federal Council acts collectively as the head of state. No single person holds supreme executive power.</li>
2564:               <li><strong>What is the significance of Abrogation of Article 370?</strong> In August 2019, the special status of J&K was revoked, and the state was bifurcated into two Union Territories.</li>
2565:             </ol>
2566:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
2567:             <ul>
2568:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Compare and contrast the Presidential system (USA) and the Parliamentary system (UK).</li>
2569:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Discuss the significance and implications of the abrogation of Article 370 for Indian federalism.</li>
2570:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Evaluate the 103rd Constitutional Amendment (EWS Quota). Does it violate the Basic Structure?</li>
2571:             </ul>
2572:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
2573:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
2574:               <p>Key constitutional systems: USA = Separation of Powers + Judicial Review. UK = Parliamentary Sovereignty + Rule of Law (Dicey). France = Semi-Presidential (5th Republic, 1958). Switzerland = Direct Democracy (Referendums).</p>
2575:             </div>
2576:           </div>
2577:         </div>

13: document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', () => {
14:   // ─── Utility: Debounce ───────────────────────────────────────────────
15:   /**
16:    * Returns a debounced version of `fn` that delays invocation
17:    * until `delay` ms have elapsed since the last call.
18:    */
19:   const debounce = (fn, delay) => {
20:     let timer = null;
21:     return (...args) => {
22:       clearTimeout(timer);
23:       timer = setTimeout(() => fn(...args), delay);
24:     };
25:   };
26: 
27:   // ─── DOM References ──────────────────────────────────────────────────
28:   const root            = document.documentElement;
29:   const sidebar         = document.getElementById('sidebar');
30:   const overlay         = document.getElementById('overlay');
31:   const hamburgerBtn    = document.getElementById('hamburger-btn');
32:   const searchInput     = document.getElementById('search-input');
33:   const searchResults   = document.getElementById('search-results');
34:   const darkModeToggle  = document.getElementById('dark-mode-toggle');
35:   const langToggle      = document.getElementById('lang-toggle');
36:   const currentTabTitle = document.getElementById('current-tab-title');
37:   const navItems        = document.querySelectorAll('.nav-item');
38:   const tabPanes        = document.querySelectorAll('.tab-pane');
39: 
40:   // ─── Constants ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────
41:   const THEME_KEY       = 'bbmku-theme';
42:   const LANG_KEY        = 'bbmku-lang';
43:   const MOBILE_BP       = 768;          // pixels
44:   const SEARCH_SNIPPET  = 50;           // chars either side of match
45:   const MAX_RESULTS     = 20;
46:   const DEBOUNCE_MS     = 300;
47: 
48:   // =====================================================================
49:   //  1. TAB SWITCHING
50:   // =====================================================================
51: 
52:   /**
53:    * Extract the display label from a nav-item element.
54:    * Grabs the icon (first child text or emoji) + the visible language span.
55:    */
56:   const getNavLabel = (navEl) => {
57:     const lang = root.dataset.lang || 'hi';
58:     const hiSpan = navEl.querySelector('.hi');
59:     const enSpan = navEl.querySelector('.en');
60:     // Visible text based on current language
61:     const text = lang === 'en'
62:       ? (enSpan ? enSpan.textContent : '')
63:       : (hiSpan ? hiSpan.textContent : '');
64: 
65:     // Try to capture leading icon / emoji that lives outside the spans
66:     let icon = '';
67:     for (const node of navEl.childNodes) {
68:       if (node.nodeType === Node.TEXT_NODE) {
69:         const trimmed = node.textContent.trim();
70:         if (trimmed) { icon = trimmed; break; }
71:       } else if (node.nodeType === Node.ELEMENT_NODE &&
72:                  !node.classList.contains('hi') &&
73:                  !node.classList.contains('en')) {
74:         icon = node.textContent.trim();
75:         break;
76:       }
77:     }
78: 
79:     return icon ? `${icon} ${text}` : text;
80:   };
81: 
82:   /**
83:    * Activate a specific tab by its ID.
84:    */
85:   const switchTab = (tabId) => {
86:     // Deactivate all nav items and tab panes
87:     navItems.forEach(n => n.classList.remove('active'));
88:     tabPanes.forEach(p => p.classList.remove('active'));
89: 
90:     // Activate the target nav item and pane
91:     const targetNav  = document.querySelector(`.nav-item[data-tab="${tabId}"]`);
92:     const targetPane = document.getElementById(tabId);
93: 
94:     if (targetNav)  targetNav.classList.add('active');
95:     if (targetPane) targetPane.classList.add('active');
96: 
97:     // Update the header title
98:     if (targetNav && currentTabTitle) {
99:       currentTabTitle.textContent = getNavLabel(targetNav);
100:     }

1252:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1253:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q5</span> Explain 'Rule of Law'.</summary>
1254:               <div class="qa-content">
1255:                 <p>A concept popularized by A.V. Dicey, meaning that <strong>no one is above the law</strong>. It entails the absolute supremacy of regular law as opposed to arbitrary power, equality before the law, and the protection of individual rights.</p>
1256:               </div>
1257:             </details>
1258: 
1259:             <h5 class="qa-section-title" style="margin-top: 20px;"><i class="fas fa-pen-nib" style="color: #3b82f6;"></i> Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</h5>
1260: 
1261:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1262:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q1</span> Critically examine the Structural-Functional approach of Gabriel Almond. <span class="qa-marks">[20 Marks]</span></summary>
1263:               <div class="qa-content">
1264:                 <h5>1. Introduction</h5>
1265:                 <p>Gabriel Almond developed the Structural-Functional approach as a tool for comparing different political systems (especially developed and developing nations) by looking at what functions they perform, rather than just their formal institutions.</p>
1266:                 <h5>2. Core Premise</h5>
1267:                 <p>Every political system has certain structures (institutions like parties, courts) that perform specific functions. To understand a system, we must ask: "What structures perform what functions?"</p>
1268:                 <h5>3. Input Functions (Performed by society/non-state actors)</h5>
1269:                 <ul>
1270:                   <li><strong>Political Socialization & Recruitment:</strong> Inducting people into political roles (Family, Schools).</li>
1271:                   <li><strong>Interest Articulation:</strong> Expressing demands (Pressure Groups).</li>
1272:                   <li><strong>Interest Aggregation:</strong> Combining demands into policy alternatives (Political Parties).</li>
1273:                   <li><strong>Political Communication:</strong> Flow of information (Media).</li>
1274:                 </ul>
1275:                 <h5>4. Output Functions (Performed by the state)</h5>
1276:                 <ul>
1277:                   <li><strong>Rule-making:</strong> Making laws (Legislature).</li>
1278:                   <li><strong>Rule-application:</strong> Implementing laws (Executive/Bureaucracy).</li>
1279:                   <li><strong>Rule-adjudication:</strong> Resolving disputes (Judiciary).</li>
1280:                 </ul>
1281:                 <h5>5. Criticism</h5>
1282:                 <p>Critics argue it suffers from a Western bias (ethnocentrism), assuming the Anglo-American democratic model is the ideal. It is also criticized for focusing too much on systemic stability and ignoring revolutionary change.</p>
1283:               </div>
1284:             </details>
1285: 
1286:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1287:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q2</span> Discuss the theories of Political Development formulated by Lucian Pye and Samuel Huntington. <span class="qa-marks">[20 Marks]</span></summary>
1288:               <div class="qa-content">
1289:                 <h5>1. Introduction</h5>
1290:                 <p>In the 1960s, political scientists sought to understand how newly independent nations of the "Third World" modernize politically. Pye and Huntington provided the most influential frameworks.</p>
1291:                 <h5>2. Lucian Pye's Development Syndrome</h5>
1292:                 <p>Pye identified three core characteristics of political development (the "Development Syndrome"):</p>
1293:                 <ul>
1294:                   <li><strong>Equality:</strong> Mass participation, universal laws, and recruitment based on achievement rather than birth.</li>
1295:                   <li><strong>Capacity:</strong> The government's ability to manage public affairs, enforce laws, and manage tensions effectively.</li>
1296:                   <li><strong>Differentiation:</strong> Specialization of political roles and structures (e.g., separation of judiciary and executive).</li>
1297:                 </ul>
1298:                 <h5>3. Samuel Huntington's Institutionalization Theory</h5>
1299:                 <p>Huntington challenged the optimistic view that economic modernization naturally leads to political development. In <em>'Political Order in Changing Societies'</em>, he argued:</p>
1300:                 <ul>
1301:                   <li>Rapid social mobilization without adequate political institutions leads to <strong>Political Decay</strong> (chaos, coups, instability).</li>
1302:                   <li>Political development is defined as the <strong>institutionalization</strong> of political organizations and procedures (adaptability, complexity, autonomy, coherence).</li>
1303:                   <li>Order must precede democracy in developing nations.</li>
1304:                 </ul>
1305:                 <h5>4. Conclusion</h5>
1306:                 <p>While Pye focused on the qualitative characteristics of a developed polity, Huntington focused on the painful process of achieving stability, making his theory highly relevant for analyzing modern fragile states.</p>
1307:               </div>
1308:             </details>
1309: 
1310:             <details class="qa-accordion">
1311:               <summary><span class="qa-badge">Q3</span> Compare the Presidential system of the USA with the Parliamentary system of the UK. <span class="qa-marks">[15 Marks]</span></summary>
1312:               <div class="qa-content">
1313:                 <h5>1. Introduction</h5>
1314:                 <p>The USA and UK represent the two classic democratic models, differing fundamentally in the relationship between the executive and legislative branches.</p>
1315:                 <h5>2. Separation of Powers vs. Fusion of Powers</h5>
1316:                 <ul>
1317:                   <li><strong>USA (Presidential):</strong> Strict Separation of Powers. The President (Executive) is elected separately from Congress (Legislature). They have separate tenures and cannot be members of each other's branches.</li>
1318:                   <li><strong>UK (Parliamentary):</strong> Fusion of Powers. The Prime Minister and Cabinet are drawn from the Parliament (Legislature) and sit in it.</li>
1319:                 </ul>
1320:                 <h5>3. Head of State and Government</h5>
1321:                 <ul>
1322:                   <li><strong>USA:</strong> The President is both the ceremonial Head of State and the actual Head of Government.</li>
1323:                   <li><strong>UK:</strong> The Monarch is the ceremonial Head of State, while the Prime Minister is the real Head of Government.</li>
1324:                 </ul>
1325:                 <h5>4. Accountability and Tenure</h5>
1326:                 <ul>
1327:                   <li><strong>USA:</strong> The President serves a fixed 4-year term and cannot be removed by Congress on a vote of no-confidence (only via difficult impeachment for crimes).</li>
1328:                   <li><strong>UK:</strong> The Prime Minister relies on the continuous support of the Parliament. A 'Vote of No Confidence' can remove the government immediately.</li>
1329:                 </ul>
1330:                 <h5>5. Conclusion</h5>
1331:                 <p>The US system prioritizes checks and balances and stability, sometimes leading to gridlock. The UK system prioritizes efficiency and accountability, but can lead to "elective dictatorship" if the majority is large.</p>
1332:               </div>
1333:             </details>

1338:             </div>

76: 868:           <!-- PAPER 1 (FC-101 / PSC-F-101) -->
77: 869:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Political Theory (राजनीतिक सिद्धांत)</h4>
78: 870:           <div class="content-box">
79: 871:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
80: 872:             <ol>
81: 873:               <li><strong>What is the 'Post-Behavioral Revolution'?</strong> Led by David Easton, focusing on 'Action' and 'Relevance' to solve real-world problems.</li>
82: 874:               <li><strong>Explain John Rawls' 'Veil of Ignorance'.</strong> A thought experiment where individuals design a just society without knowing their status.</li>
83: 875:               <li><strong>Define 'Negative Liberty'.</strong> The absence of external constraints (Hobbes, Berlin).</li>
84: 876:               <li><strong>What is 'Multiculturalism'?</strong> A political philosophy that accommodates cultural differences of minority groups.</li>
85: 877:               <li><strong>What is 'Hegemony' (Gramsci)?</strong> Ideological domination of the ruling class through manufactured consent.</li>
86: 878:             </ol>
87: 879:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
88: 880:             <ul>
89: 881:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Examine the debate on the 'Decline and Resurgence' of Political Theory. (Focus: Easton, Laslett, Rawls).</li>
90: 882:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Critically analyze John Rawls' Theory of Justice. (Focus: Two Principles, Difference Principle).</li>
91: 883:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Compare Negative and Positive Liberty with reference to Isaiah Berlin.</li>
92: 884:             </ul>
93: 885:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
94: 886:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
95: 887:               <p>Memorize Isaiah Berlin's 1958 essay "Two Concepts of Liberty". Know Peter Laslett's quote: "Political philosophy is dead."</p>
96: 888:             </div>
97: 889:           </div>
98: 890: 
99: 891:           <!-- PAPER 2 (CC-102 / PSC-C-103) -->
100: 892:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Western Political Thought (पाश्चात्य राजनीतिक विचार)</h4>
101: 893:           <div class="content-box">
102: 894:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
103: 895:             <ol>
104: 896:               <li><strong>What is Plato's concept of 'Philosopher King'?</strong> A ruler with true knowledge, free from family/property ties.</li>
105: 897:               <li><strong>Define Aristotle's 'Distributive Justice'.</strong> Distribution of offices according to merit (geometric proportion).</li>
106: 898:               <li><strong>What is Hobbes' 'State of Nature'?</strong> "War of every man against every man"; life is solitary, poor, nasty, brutish, and short.</li>
107: 899:               <li><strong>What is J.S. Mill's 'Harm Principle'?</strong> State interference is only justified to prevent harm to others.</li>
108: 900:               <li><strong>Define Marx's 'Historical Materialism'.</strong> Material conditions (base) determine the social and political structure (superstructure).</li>
109: 901:             </ol>
110: 902:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
111: 903:             <ul>
112: 904:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Compare and contrast the Social Contract theories of Hobbes, Locke, and Rousseau.</li>
113: 905:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Analyze Karl Marx's critique of Capitalism and his vision of a Communist society.</li>
114: 906:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Evaluate Rousseau's paradox: "Man is forced to be free."</li>
115: 907:             </ul>
116: 908:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
117: 909:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
118: 910:               <p>Chronology is King! Arrange Plato's books (Republic, Statesman, Laws) in order. Understand the difference between Hegel's Dialectical Idealism and Marx's Dialectical Materialism.</p>
119: 911:             </div>
120: 912:           </div>
121: 913: 
122: 914:           <!-- PAPER 3 (CC-103 / PSC-C-102) -->
123: 915:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Indian Political Thought (भारतीय राजनीतिक विचार)</h4>
124: 916:           <div class="content-box">
125: 917:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
126: 918:             <ol>
127: 919:               <li><strong>Explain Kautilya's concept of 'Amatya'.</strong> High-ranking officials/ministers in the Saptanga theory.</li>
128: 920:               <li><strong>What is the 'Drain Theory'?</strong> Dadabhai Naoroji's theory that British rule systematically drained India's wealth.</li>
129: 921:               <li><strong>Define Gandhi's 'Trusteeship'.</strong> Wealthy individuals act as 'trustees', using surplus for societal welfare.</li>
130: 922:               <li><strong>What is 'Radical Humanism'?</strong> M.N. Roy's philosophy focusing on individual reason and freedom, rejecting Marxism.</li>
131: 923:               <li><strong>What is 'Annihilation of Caste'?</strong> B.R. Ambedkar's call to destroy the caste system and its religious texts.</li>
132: 924:             </ol>
133: 925:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
134: 926:             <ul>
135: 927:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Critically examine Kautilya's Saptanga Theory of State and Mandala Theory.</li>
136: 928:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Evaluate the debate between Gandhi and Ambedkar on the issue of Caste and Untouchability.</li>
137: 929:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Analyze the political philosophy of Bal Gangadhar Tilak (Swaraj, Nationalism).</li>
138: 930:             </ul>
139: 931:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
140: 932:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
141: 933:               <p>Differentiate ideological clashes (Gandhi vs Ambedkar, Tilak vs Gokhale). Memorize journals (Mooknayak, Harijan, Young India).</p>
142: 934:             </div>
143: 935:           </div>
144: 936: 
145: 937:           <!-- PAPER 4 (CC-104 / PSC-C-104) -->
146: 938:           <h4 class="unit-title" style="color: #6366f1;">Comparative Politics (तुलनात्मक राजनीति)</h4>
147: 939:           <div class="content-box">
148: 940:             <p><strong>Top 5 Short Questions (2-5 Marks)</strong></p>
149: 941:             <ol>
150: 942:               <li><strong>Define David Easton's 'Input-Output Model'.</strong> A system where 'inputs' (demands) are converted into 'outputs' (policies).</li>
151: 943:               <li><strong>What is 'Interest Articulation'?</strong> Expressing demands to decision-makers (done by pressure groups).</li>
152: 944:               <li><strong>What is 'Political Culture'?</strong> Almond and Verba's concept (Parochial, Subject, Participant cultures).</li>
153: 945:               <li><strong>Differentiate Federal and Unitary systems.</strong> Federal divides power (USA, India); Unitary centralizes power (UK).</li>
154: 946:               <li><strong>Explain 'Rule of Law'.</strong> No one is above the law (A.V. Dicey).</li>
155: 947:             </ol>
156: 948:             <p><strong>Top 3 Long Questions (15-20 Marks)</strong></p>
157: 949:             <ul>
158: 950:               <li><strong>Q1.</strong> Critically examine the Structural-Functional approach of Gabriel Almond.</li>
159: 951:               <li><strong>Q2.</strong> Discuss the theories of Political Development formulated by Lucian Pye and Samuel Huntington.</li>
160: 952:               <li><strong>Q3.</strong> Compare the Presidential system of the USA with the Parliamentary system of the UK.</li>
161: 953:             </ul>
162: 954:             <div class="info-box" style="border-left-color: #f59e0b;">
163: 955:               <h4>🎓 UGC NET Expert Tips</h4>
164: 956:               <p>Memorize the 5 countries in 'The Civic Culture' (USA, UK, Germany, Italy, Mexico). Match Almond's structures correctly (Interest Articulation = Pressure Groups).</p>
165: 957:             </div>
166: 958:           </div>
167: 959:         </div>
168: 960:       </div>

228: 1020:         <div class="paper-section">
229: 1021:           <h3 class="paper-title"><span class="hi">PSC-C-206: अंतर्राष्ट्रीय राजनीति के सिद्धांत</span><span
230: 1022:               class="en">PSC-C-206: Theories of International Politics</span></h3>
231: 1023: 
232: 1024:           <h4 class="unit-title"><span class="hi">इकाई 2: उपागम — यथार्थवाद (Realism)</span><span class="en">Unit 2:
233: 1025:               Approaches — Realism</span></h4>
234: 1026:           <p><span class="hi">अंतर्राष्ट्रीय संबंधों में प्रमुख प्रतिमान (Paradigm)। प्रमुख मान्यताएँ: राज्य प्राथमिक
235: 1027:               कर्ता हैं, अंतर्राष्ट्रीय व्यवस्था अराजक है (कोई विश्व सरकार नहीं), राज्य तर्कसंगत रूप से राष्ट्रीय हित
236: 1028:               (शक्ति) की पूर्ति करते हैं, और नैतिकता का कोई विशेष स्थान नहीं है।</span><span class="en">The dominant
237: 1029:               paradigm in International Relations. Key assumptions: States are the primary actors, the international
238: 1030:               system is anarchic (no world government), states rationally pursue national interest (power), and morality
239: 1031:               has no significant place.</span></p>
240: 1032:           <ul>
241: 1033:             <li><strong><span class="hi">हंस मोर्गेन्थाऊ (शास्त्रीय यथार्थवाद):</span><span class="en">Hans Morgenthau
242: 1034:                   (Classical Realism):</span></strong> <span class="hi">आधुनिक यथार्थवाद के जनक। पुस्तक: <em>'पॉलिटिक्स
243: 1035:                   अमंग नेशंस' (1948)</em>। 'शक्ति के रूप में परिभाषित राष्ट्रीय हित' इनकी मुख्य अवधारणा है।</span><span
244: 1036:                 class="en">Father of modern realism. Book: <em>'Politics Among Nations' (1948)</em>. 'National interest
245: 1037:                 defined in terms of power' is his core concept.</span></li>
246: 1038:             <li><strong><span class="hi">थ्यूसीडाइड्स:</span><span class="en">Thucydides:</span></strong> <span
247: 1039:                 class="hi">प्राचीन ग्रीक इतिहासकार (पेलोपोनेसियन युद्ध)। मेलियन संवाद (Melian Dialogue): "शक्तिशाली वही
248: 1040:                 करते हैं जो वे कर सकते हैं और कमज़ोर वही सहते हैं जो उन्हें सहना पड़ता है।"</span><span
249: 1041:                 class="en">Ancient Greek historian (Peloponnesian War). Melian Dialogue: "The strong do what they can
250: 1042:                 and the weak suffer what they must."</span></li>
251: 1043:             <li><strong><span class="hi">नव-यथार्थवाद / संरचनात्मक यथार्थवाद (केनेथ वाल्ट्ज़):</span><span
252: 1044:                   class="en">Neo-Realism / Structural Realism (Kenneth Waltz):</span></strong> <span class="hi">पुस्तक:
253: 1045:                 <em>'थ्योरी ऑफ इंटरनेशनल पॉलिटिक्स' (1979)</em>। इन्होंने राज्यों के इरादों के बजाय अंतर्राष्ट्रीय
254: 1046:                 व्यवस्था की 'अराजक संरचना' पर ध्यान केंद्रित किया।</span><span class="en">Book: <em>'Theory of
255: 1047:                   International Politics' (1979)</em>. Focused on the 'anarchic structure' of the international system
256: 1048:                 rather than the intentions of states.</span></li>
257: 1049:           </ul>
258: 1050: 
259: 1051:           <h4 class="unit-title"><span class="hi">इकाई 5 से 9: शक्ति संतुलन, सामूहिक सुरक्षा एवं
260: 1052:               गुटनिरपेक्षता</span><span class="en">Unit 5 to 9: Balance of Power, Collective Security & NAM</span></h4>
261: 1053:           <ul>
262: 1054:             <li><strong><span class="hi">शक्ति संतुलन (Balance of Power):</span><span class="en">Balance of
263: 1055:                   Power:</span></strong> <span class="hi">ऐसी स्थिति जहाँ कोई भी एक राज्य अत्यधिक हावी नहीं हो पाता।
264: 1056:                 राज्य अपनी सुरक्षा और स्वतंत्रता को बनाए रखने के लिए गठबंधन (Alliances) बनाते हैं।</span><span
265: 1057:                 class="en">A situation where no single state becomes overly dominant. States form alliances to maintain
266: 1058:                 their security and independence.</span></li>
267: 1059:             <li><strong><span class="hi">सामूहिक सुरक्षा (Collective Security):</span><span class="en">Collective
268: 1060:                   Security:</span></strong> <span class="hi">यह सिद्धांत कि "एक पर हमला सभी पर हमला है" (One for all,
269: 1061:                 all for one)। यह राष्ट्र संघ (League of Nations) और संयुक्त राष्ट्र चार्टर (अध्याय VII) का आधार
270: 1062:                 है।</span><span class="en">The principle that "an attack on one is an attack on all" (One for all, all
271: 1063:                 for one). This is the basis of the League of Nations and the UN Charter (Chapter VII).</span></li>
272: 1064:             <li><strong><span class="hi">गुटनिरपेक्षता (NAM):</span><span class="en">Non-Aligned Movement
273: 1065:                   (NAM):</span></strong> <span class="hi">शीत युद्ध के दौरान किसी भी सैन्य गठबंधन (NATO या वारसा पैक्ट)
274: 1066:                 में शामिल न होने की विदेश नीति। बांडुंग सम्मेलन (1955) इसके लिए प्रारंभिक कदम था; इसे औपचारिक रूप से
275: 1067:                 बेलग्रेड (1961) में शुरू किया गया था।</span><span class="en">The foreign policy of not joining any
276: 1068:                 military alliance (NATO or Warsaw Pact) during the Cold War. The Bandung Conference (1955) was the
277: 1069:                 preliminary step; it was formally launched in Belgrade (1961).</span></li>
278: 1070:           </ul>
279: 1071:         </div>
280: 1072: 
281: 1073:         <!-- Paper 207 -->
282: 1074:         <div class="paper-section">
283: 1075:           <h3 class="paper-title"><span class="hi">PSC-C-207: लोक प्रशासन</span><span class="en">PSC-C-207: Public
284: 1076:               Administration</span></h3>
285: 1077: 
286: 1078:           <h4 class="unit-title"><span class="hi">इकाई 2: लोक प्रशासन के प्रमुख सिद्धांत</span><span class="en">Unit 2:
287: 1079:               Major Theories of Public Administration</span></h4>
288: 1080:           <ul>
289: 1081:             <li><strong><span class="hi">मानवीय संबंध सिद्धांत — एल्टन मेयो:</span><span class="en">Human Relations
290: 1082:                   Theory — Elton Mayo:</span></strong> <span class="hi"><strong>हाथॉर्न प्रयोग (1924–32)</strong> ने
291: 1083:                 साबित किया कि कार्यस्थल पर उत्पादकता केवल भौतिक परिस्थितियों (रोशनी/पैसे) पर नहीं, बल्कि सामाजिक कारकों,
292: 1084:                 कार्यकर्ता के मनोबल और अनौपचारिक समूहों (Informal groups) पर निर्भर करती है।</span><span class="en">The
293: 1085:                 <strong>Hawthorne Experiments (1924–32)</strong> proved that workplace productivity depends not only on
294: 1086:                 physical conditions (lighting/money) but on social factors, worker morale, and informal groups.</span>
295: 1087:             </li>
296: 1088:             <li><strong><span class="hi">निर्णय-निर्माण सिद्धांत — हर्बर्ट साइमन:</span><span class="en">Decision-Making
297: 1089:                   Theory — Herbert Simon:</span></strong> <span class="hi">'प्रशासनिक व्यवहार' (1947)। प्रमुख अवधारणा:
298: 1090:                 <strong>परिसीमित तर्कसंगतता (Bounded Rationality)</strong>। साइमन के अनुसार निर्णय निर्माता असीमित
299: 1091:                 जानकारी नहीं रखते, इसलिए वे 'इष्टतम' (Optimize) करने के बजाय 'संतोषजनक' (Satisficing) विकल्प चुनते
300: 1092:                 हैं।</span><span class="en">'Administrative Behavior' (1947). Core concept: <strong>Bounded
301: 1093:                   Rationality</strong>. Simon argued that decision-makers lack unlimited information, so they choose a
302: 1094:                 'satisficing' option instead of an 'optimizing' one.</span></li>
303: 1095:             <li><strong><span class="hi">पारिस्थितिक सिद्धांत — एफ. डब्ल्यू. रिग्स:</span><span class="en">Ecological
304: 1096:                   Theory — F. W. Riggs:</span></strong> <span class="hi">विकासशील देशों के प्रशासन को समझाने के लिए
305: 1097:                 <strong>प्रिज़्मेटिक-साला मॉडल (Prismatic-Sala Model)</strong> विकसित किया। (फ्यूज्ड → प्रिज़्मेटिक →
306: 1098:                 डिफ्रैक्टेड)।</span><span class="en">Developed the <strong>Prismatic-Sala Model</strong> to explain
307: 1099:                 administration in developing countries. (Fused → Prismatic → Diffracted).</span></li>
308: 1100:           </ul>
